The Scrolls of Deeds: Reconciling Hadiths
The commentator explains the scrolls of deeds and reconciles hadiths about how they are given.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the meaning of the scrolls of deeds and how apparent contradictions between hadiths about their delivery are reconciled.

Core Idea
The scrolls of deeds are for all people, and hadiths are reconciled by angels placing them from the necks into hands.

This passage from the Samiyyat section tackles the scrolls of deeds and resolves a seeming conflict between hadiths. One hadith says the wind brings scrolls from under the Throne; another says angels give them. The commentator clarifies that both are true: the angels take them from the necks and place them in hands, harmonizing the accounts.

Guided Path
1
Understand 'scrolls'
Read the opening: the scrolls are the books in which angels recorded deeds. They are not only for angels or prophets but for all people.
The plural 'scrolls' corresponds to the multitude of servants.
2
Identify the apparent conflict
Note the two reports: one says wind blows scrolls from under the Throne to each person's neck; another says every person is called and given his book. The commentator notes that the author did not specify a cause due to this apparent diversity.
This diversity could cause confusion about how the scrolls are actually given.
3
Learn the reconciliation
The commentator resolves: angels take the scrolls from the necks and place them in the hands. This combines both accounts: the wind brings them to the necks, then angels complete the delivery.
This reconciliation shows how the sound hadiths are harmonized.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قسم السمعيات ولا الملائكة ولا الأنبياء فإنهم لا يأخذون الصحفا المراد منها الكتب التي كتبت الملائكة فيها ما فعلوه في الدنيا وعلى هذا فقيل توصل صحف الأيام والليالي وقيل ينسخ ما في جميعها في صحيفة واحدة وجمع الصحف لمقابلة العباد ولم يذكر المصنف رحمه الله تعالى دافع جمع الصحف لما ورد أن الريح تطيرها من خزانة تحت العرش فلا تخطئ صحيفة عنق صاحبها وأن كل أحد يدعى فيعطى كتابه وجمع بأن الملائكة تأخذها من الأعناق وتضعها في الأيدي والآيات والأحاديث شاهدة بعمومه لجميع الأمم
The section of Samiyyat. And not the angels nor the prophets, for they do not take the scrolls. What is meant by them is the books in which the angels wrote what they did in the world. On this basis, it is said: the scrolls of days and nights are joined together, and it is said: what is in all of them is copied into one scroll. And he mentioned 'the scrolls' in plural to correspond to the plural of servants. And the author, may Allah have mercy on him, did not mention the cause of the gathering of the scrolls because of what is reported that the wind blows them from a treasure under the Throne, so no scroll misses the neck of its owner, and that every person is called and given his book. And it is reconciled by saying that the angels take them from the necks and place them in the hands. And the verses and hadiths are witnesses to its generality for all nations.
Source pages p. 533

Commentary
This passage is an explanation of the samiyyat section, specifically addressing the taking of the scrolls of deeds. The commentator first clarifies that the scrolls are for all people, not only for angels or prophets. He then explains that the plural 'scrolls' is used to correspond to the multitude of servants. He notes that the author did not mention the means by which the scrolls are given, due to conflicting reports: one hadith says the wind carries them from under the Throne to each person's neck, another says angels give them. The commentator resolves this by saying that the angels take them from the necks and place them in the hands. He concludes that both verses and hadiths attest that all nations will receive their books in this manner.

Key Terms
الصحف
السمعيات
الريح
العرش
الملائكة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the scrolls are only for believers or specific groups.
Correction: The commentator explicitly states that the verses and hadiths witness to its generality for all nations.

Checkpoint
How does the commentator reconcile the hadith that the wind brings the scrolls with the hadith that angels give them?
A) He accepts only the wind hadith and rejects the angel hadith.
B) He says the angels take them from the necks and place them in the hands.
C) He says the wind carries them directly to the hands.
D) He says both are true but for different people.

Key Takeaway
The scrolls of deeds are for all people, and the hadiths are reconciled by the angels transferring them from the necks to the hands.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Every deed you do is recorded in a scroll that you will hold on a day that is surely coming. If you were handed your scroll right now, what would you see? What deed from today would you be most ashamed to find, and what can you do right now to erase or change it before you meet your book?
?
The wind does not miss a single person's neck—your scroll will find you no matter what. Do you live as though that moment is imminent? Write down one habit you need to abandon today so that when you receive your scroll, you find it lighter in the places that matter most.
?
The angels take the scroll from your neck and place it in your hand—there is no escape from the reckoning. If the angels handed you your record and said 'This is your truth,' would you be at peace or terrified? Commit to one concrete action this week that will make you long to see your scroll rather than dread it.

Quranic Evidence for Receiving the Book
The commentator cites Quranic verses to establish that believers and disbelievers receive their books differently.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Quranic evidence for how believers and disbelievers receive their books, and the ruling for the sinful believer.

Core Idea
The Quran itself distinguishes believers and disbelievers by which hand receives their book.

The commentator grounds the doctrine of receiving the book in explicit Quranic verses. By examining Surah Al-Haqqa, we see clear evidence for the obedient believer and the disbeliever. The status of the sinful believer is then clarified by the scholar Al-Mawardi, showing that even the sinful believer receives his book in the right hand as a sign of eventual salvation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Let the text's own structure come through before you analyze.
Pay attention to the Quranic verses cited.
2
Identify the two Quranic verses
Find the verses from Surah Al-Haqqa. Notice what each verse indicates: one for the obedient believer (right hand) and one for the disbeliever (left hand).
The verses are explicit and form the core evidence.
3
Examine the ruling for the sinful believer
Read Al-Mawardi's decisive ruling that the sinful believer also receives his book in the right hand, and understand the reasoning: it is a sign of not remaining forever in the Fire.
This clarifies a potential misunderstanding.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فيأخذون كما من القرآن نصا أي منصوصا عرفا أي أخذا مماثلا لما عرف تفصيله من نص القرآن كقوله تعالى: {فَأَمَّا مَنْ أُوتِيَ كِتَابَهُ بِيَمِينِهِ فَيَقُولُ هَاؤُمُ اقْرَءُوا كِتَابِيَهْ إِنِّي ظَنَنْتُ أَنِّي مُلَاقٍ حِسَابِيَهْ} [الحاقة: 20] الآية، {وَأَمَّا مَنْ أُوتِيَ كِتَابَهُ بِشِمَالِهِ فَيَقُولُ يَا لَيْتَنِي لَمْ أُوتَ كِتَابِيَهْ} [الحاقة: 25] دلت الآية بحسب أولها على أن المؤمن الطائع يأخذ كتابه بيمينه، وبحسب آخرها على أن آخذه بشماله هو الكافر، وأما المؤمن الفاسق فجزم الماوردي بأنه يأخذه بيمينه، قال: وهو المشهور، فقيل: يأخذه قبل دخول النار، ويكون ذلك علامة على عدم الخلود.
So they take it as is from the Quran, a text, i.e., a known text, i.e., a taking similar to what is known in detail from the text of the Quran, such as His saying the Exalted: 'Then as for he who is given his book in his right hand, he will say, "Here, read my book! Indeed, I was certain that I would be meeting my account."' [Al-Haqqa:20] and His saying: 'But as for he who is given his book in his left hand, he will say, "Oh, I wish I had not been given my book."' [Al-Haqqa:25]. The verse indicates, according to its first part, that the obedient believer takes his book with his right hand, and according to its last part, that the one who takes it with his left is the disbeliever. As for the sinful believer, Al-Mawardi decisively stated that he takes it with his right hand. He said: And it is the well-known view. So it is said: He takes it before entering the Fire, and that is a sign of not remaining forever.
Source pages p. 533

Commentary
This passage provides the Quranic evidence for the manner of receiving the book, and then elaborates on the cases. The commentator begins by stating that the people take their books as explicitly stated in the Quran, citing two verses from Surah Al-Haqqa. The first verse shows the obedient believer receiving his book in his right hand, and the second shows the disbeliever receiving in his left. The commentator then addresses the case of the sinful believer, citing Al-Mawardi's decisive view that he also receives his book in his right hand, which is the well-known opinion. This is explained by the fact that he receives it before entering the Fire, serving as a sign that he will not remain in it forever.

Key Terms
كتاب
يمين
شمال
مؤمن فاسق
الماوردي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think the sinful believer receives his book in the left hand like the disbeliever.
Correction: Al-Mawardi confirms that the sinful believer receives his book in the right hand, before entering the Fire, as a sign of eventual salvation.

Checkpoint
According to Al-Mawardi, when does the sinful believer receive his book in the right hand?
A) After entering the Fire.
B) Before entering the Fire.
C) At the same time as the disbeliever.
D) He does not receive a book.

Key Takeaway
The Quran clearly shows the obedient believer receives his book in the right hand and the disbeliever in the left; the sinful believer also receives in the right hand, signaling eventual salvation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you imagine standing before Allah on Judgment Day, which hand do you truly fear receiving your book in—and why? What does your daily life say about which hand you deserve?
?
The sinful believer still receives the book in the right hand as a sign of hope. Are you relying on that hope while neglecting your duties? What specific sin are you holding onto because you assume you'll still be saved?
?
Al-Mawardi's view that the sinful believer receives the book before entering the Fire gives a moment of reckoning before punishment. How does that change your understanding of Allah's justice and mercy? Will you change anything today because of it?

The Distribution of Books on the Day of Judgment
Explains first recipients and nature of reading.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the details of the distribution of the books of deeds on the Day of Judgment, including the first recipients in the right and left hands and the nature of the reading.

Core Idea
The books of deeds are given to each person; the first to receive in the right hand is Umar, and the reading is literal for all, even the illiterate.

This passage from the commentary on al-Jawhara discusses the sam'iyyat concerning the distribution of books on the Day of Judgment. It highlights key figures and the nature of the reading, clarifying a common misunderstanding. Let's delve into the text to understand these eschatological events.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without pausing, then read the full English translation. Let the author's rhythm and key terms stand out.
Notice the names mentioned: al-Khattab, Abu 'Umar ibn Salamah, and al-Aswad.
2
Identify the first recipients
The passage lists who receives the book in the right hand first, and who receives it in the left hand first. Mark these names and understand their significance.
The first to receive in the right hand is Umar al-Khattab, not the Prophet.
3
Understand the debate on reading
The passage presents two views on the reading of the book: real (haqiqi) and metaphorical (majazi). Identify which view is preferred and why.
The preferred view is that it is a real, literal reading, not just knowledge.
4
Reflect on the miracle
The passage states that everyone will read their own book, even if they were illiterate. Consider what this implies about the nature of the Hereafter.
This shows Allah's power and the individual accountability.
5
Connect to broader lessons
Think about how this teaching reinforces the importance of deeds and the certainty of Judgement Day.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قسم السمعيات. مطلقا وأوَّلُ مَن يُعطى كتابه بيمينه الخطاب، وبعده أبو عمر بن سلمة عبد الله بن عبد الأسد، وأخوه الأسود بن عبد الأسد أوَّلُ مَن يأخذه بشماله. القراءة حقيقيَّة، وقيل: مجازية، عُبر بها عن علم كلِّ أحد بِمَا لَهُ وَمَا عَلَيْهِ، ويَقرأ كلُّ أحدٍ كتابه ولو كان أميًّا.
Section of the audible things. Absolutely, and the first person to be given his book in his right hand is al-Khattab (Umar), and after him Abu 'Umar ibn Salamah 'Abdullah ibn 'Abd al-Asad, and his brother al-Aswad ibn 'Abd al-Asad is the first to take it in his left hand. The reading is real, and it is said: metaphorical, expressed by it for the knowledge of everyone of what is for him and what is against him, and everyone reads his book even if he was illiterate.
Source pages p. 535

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the sam'iyyat (audible things) concerning the distribution of the books of deeds on the Day of Judgment. It first identifies the first person from the ummah to receive his book in his right hand as Umar ibn al-Khattab (al-Khattab here refers to him), followed by Abu 'Umar ibn Salamah, and then his brother al-Aswad who is the first to receive his book in his left hand. The commentary then discusses the nature of the 'reading' of the book: the preferred view is that it is a real, literal reading (haqiqiyya), though some say it is metaphorical (majaziyya), meaning that each person will know his deeds. Importantly, every person will read his own book, even if he was illiterate in this world, emphasizing the miraculous nature of that event.

Key Terms
سمعيات
كتاب
يمين
شمال
قراءة حقيقية
قراءة مجازية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the reading of the book is merely metaphorical, meaning it is not an actual reading but only an inner knowledge.
Correction: The text states 'القراءة حقيقية' (the reading is real), indicating that the preferred and correct belief is that it is a literal reading, though some scholars held the metaphorical interpretation.

Checkpoint
According to the commentary, who is the first person to receive his book in the right hand on the Day of Judgment?
A) Prophet Muhammad
B) Abu Bakr
C) Umar al-Khattab
D) Ali ibn Abi Talib

Key Takeaway
On the Day of Judgment, each person will literally read his own book of deeds, even if illiterate, and the first from the ummah to receive his book in the right hand is Umar ibn al-Khattab.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If your book of deeds were placed in your hands right now, would you expect it in your right or left? What does your answer reveal about your current state of faith and action, and what will you change today to ensure it is in your right hand?
?
Umar ibn al-Khattab, despite his past in Jahiliyyah, became the first of this ummah to receive his book in the right hand. What does this tell you about the power of sincere repentance and action? Is there any sin or habit you have been using as an excuse to avoid changing?
?
The fact that every person—even the illiterate—will literally read their own book shows that Allah will make the truth undeniable on that day. Are you living now as if every deed is being recorded and will be read by you? What is one deed you will consciously do today to add to your right-hand record?

The Weighing of Deeds and the Balance
Defines the weighing of deeds and the balance, citing Quranic proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the weighing of deeds on the Day of Judgment is a literal, sensory event supported by Quranic evidence, and that belief in it is an auditory obligation.

Core Idea
The balance of deeds is a real scale, not a metaphor.

In this passage, the author explains a key event of the Hereafter: the weighing of deeds. He defines it as a literal weighing using a sensory balance, and supports this with clear Quranic verses. This lesson unpacks that definition and the proof texts.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the translation. Notice the flow from definition to proof to linguistic explanation.
2
Identify the definition of weighing and balance
The passage defines 'weighing' as the weighing of deeds and 'balance' as a sensory tool. Mark these definitions.
The phrase 'آلة حسية' is key.
3
Examine the Quranic proofs
Three verses are cited: 7:8, 21:47, and 23:102-103. Note how each verse reinforces the reality of the weighing.
The third verse describes the outcomes of heavy vs light scales.
4
Reflect on the linguistic definition
The passage ends with the linguistic meaning of 'wazn'. Consider how this aligns with the sensory balance.
5
Address the misconception
Some think the balance is metaphorical. The passage explicitly calls it a sensory tool, so it is literal.
This is a common misunderstanding to avoid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَزِنُ الأعمال.
وَمِثْلُ هَذا الوَزْنُ والميزانُ فَتُوزَنُ الكُتُبُ أو الأعْيانُ.
(وَمِثْلُ هَذَا الوَزْنُ وَالمِيزَانُ) أي: وزنُ أعمال العبادِ، والآلةُ الحِسيَّة التي يوزنُ بها مثل أخذ العباد كتب أعمالهم في الوجوبِ السَّمعي وتَحتُّمِ الإيمان به، قال تعالى: ﴿وَالْوَزْنُ يَوْمَيذٍ الْحَقُّ ﴾ [الأعراف: ۸]، ﴿وَنَضَعُ الْمَوَازِينَ الْقِسْطَ لِيَوْمِ الْقِيَمَةِ ﴾ [الأنبياء: ٤٧]، فَمَن ثَقُلَتْ مَوَازِينُهُ فَأُولَتَبِكَ هُمُ الْمُفْلِحُونَ وَمَنْ خَفَّتْ مَوَازِينُهُ فَأُولَبِكَ الَّذِينَ خَسِرُوا أَنفُسَهُمْ فِي جَهَنَّمَ خَالِدُونَ ﴾ [المؤمنون: ۱۰۲ - ۱۰۳] والوزن لغةً: معرفةُ كَمِّيَّة بأخرى على وجه مخصُوص.
And the weighing of deeds. And like this is the weighing and the balance, so the books or the deeds are weighed. (And like this is the weighing and the balance): i.e., the weighing of the deeds of the servants, and the sensory tool by which it is weighed, like the taking of the servants' books of their deeds, in the auditory obligation and the necessity of believing in it. He said, the Most High: "And the weighing on that Day is the truth" [al-A'raf: 8], "And We shall set up the balances of justice for the Day of Resurrection" [al-Anbiya': 47], "So those whose scales are heavy, they are the successful, and those whose scales are light, they are the ones who have lost their souls, in Hell abiding" [al-Mu'minun: 102-103]. And weighing linguistically: the knowledge of a quantity by another in a specific manner.
Source pages p. 536

Commentary
This passage is a definition and proof of the weighing of deeds on the Day of Judgment. It begins with a line from the poem: 'And like this is the weighing and the balance, so the books or the deeds are weighed.' The commentary then explains that 'weighing' here means the weighing of the servants' deeds, and the 'balance' is a sensory tool (a physical scale) by which deeds are weighed, just as the books of deeds are taken. This is an auditory obligation (wajib sam'i) that must be believed in. The commentary then cites three Quranic verses as proof: Surah al-A'raf (7:8) stating the weighing is the truth, Surah al-Anbiya (21:47) stating Allah will set up the balances of justice, and Surah al-Mu'minun (23:102-103) describing the outcomes of heavy versus light scales. Finally, it gives a linguistic definition of 'weighing' (al-wazn) as the knowledge of a quantity by another in a specific manner (i.e., comparing weights). The passage establishes the reality of the balance as a concrete event, not merely metaphorical.

Key Terms
وزن
ميزان
كتب
أعمال
حسية
وجوب سمعي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the balance is metaphorical or symbolic.
Correction: The passage explicitly calls it a 'sensory tool' (آلة حسية) and cites Quranic verses, indicating it is a literal physical scale.

Checkpoint
What is the evidence given in the passage that the weighing of deeds is a real, sensory event?
A) Linguistic analysis of the word 'wazn'.
B) Quranic verses and the definition of the balance as a sensory tool.
C) Consensus of the scholars.
D) The books are light or heavy.

Key Takeaway
The weighing of deeds on the Day of Judgment is a literal event with a sensory balance, as proven by the Quran.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If the balance of deeds is a literal scale that will tip based on your actions, what is one deed you will strive to increase in weight today, and how will you ensure it is sincere?
?
When you read 'those whose scales are light, they are the ones who have lost their souls', does that image fill you with genuine dread or has it become just words? What will you do to make that reality pierce your heart?
?
The weighing includes both your books and deeds. Is there any deed you have hidden or dismissed as insignificant that you now realize will be placed on the scale? What will you do about it before that Day?

The Reality of the Balance: Definition and Proof
Explanation of the balance (mizan) and its proof from Quran and hadith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the balance (mizan) on the Day of Judgment is a real physical instrument, proven by Quran and hadith, and that belief in it is obligatory.

Core Idea
The balance is real, not metaphorical – belief in it is mandatory.

In this passage, the author explains the reality of the balance that will weigh deeds on the Day of Judgment. He defines it both linguistically and theologically, provides clear Quranic proofs, and affirms that the hadith about it are massively transmitted (mutawatir). This establishes the balance as a core article of faith in the sam'iyyat (revelatory matters).

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and its translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the English translation to grasp the overall argument.
Pay attention to the Quranic verses quoted – they are central.
2
Identify the definition of the balance
Notice how the author defines the balance both as a physical instrument and linguistically as 'knowledge of a quantity by another'. Understand that he leaves the exact substance unspecified.
3
Examine the proofs from revelation and reason
List the three Quranic verses and note the author's claim that the hadith are mutawatir. Also note that reason (ʿaql) permits the literal interpretation.
The combination of revelation and reason makes belief obligatory.
4
Reflect on the theological stance
Understand why the author insists on a literal interpretation while refraining from specifying the nature of the balance. This protects the divine mystery while affirming the reality.
This is a common technique in kalam: affirm what is revealed without over-specifying.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمِثْلُ هَذا الوَزْنُ والميزانُ فَتُوزَنُ الكُتُبُ أو الأعْيانُ (وَمِثْلُ هَذَا الوَزْنُ وَالمِيزَانُ) أي: وزنُ أعمال العبادِ، والآلةُ الحِسيَّة التي يوزنُ بها مثل أخذ العباد كتب أعمالهم في الوجوبِ السَّمعي وتَحتُّمِ الإيمان به ، قال تعالى: ﴿وَالْوَزْنُ يَوْمَيذٍ الْحَقُّ ﴾ [الأعراف: ۸]، ﴿وَنَضَعُ الْمَوَازِينَ الْقِسْطَ لِيَوْمِ الْقِيَمَةِ ﴾ [الأنبياء: ٤٧] ، فَمَن ثَقُلَتْ مَوَازِينُهُ فَأُولَتَبِكَ هُمُ الْمُفْلِحُونَ وَمَنْ خَفَّتْ مَوَازِينُهُ فَأُولَبِكَ الَّذِينَ خَسِرُوا أَنفُسَهُمْ فِي جَهَنَّمَ خَالِدُونَ ﴾ [المؤمنون: ۱۰۲ - ۱۰۳] والوزن لغةً: معرفةُ كَمِّيَّة بأخرى على وجه مخصُوص. والحمل على الحقيقة ممكن ، لكنْ نُمسك عن تعيين نوع جوهره، وقد بلغت أحاديثه مبلغَ التَّواتر ، والعقلُ يُجوِّزه، وكلُّ ما هو كذلك فهو من مطالب هذا الفنّ ، والإيمان به وا
And like this [is] the weight and the balance: so are weighed the books or the entities. (And like this weight and balance) means: the weight of the deeds of the servants, and the physical instrument by which is weighed, like the servants taking the books of their deeds, in obligatory [belief] based on revelation and the necessity of believing in it. He (Most High) said: 'And the weight on that Day is the truth' (al-A'raf: 8), and 'And We shall set up the scales of justice for the Day of Resurrection' (al-Anbiya: 47), 'So those whose scales are heavy, they are the successful, and those whose scales are light, they are the ones who have lost their souls, in Hell abiding' (al-Mu'minun: 102-103). And weight (al-wazn) linguistically is: the knowledge of a quantity by another quantity in a specific manner. And the literal interpretation is possible, but we refrain from specifying the type of its substance, and its hadith have reached the level of tawatur (widespread transmission), and reason permits it, and everything that is thus is among the demands of this art, and belief in it is...
Source pages p. 536

Commentary
This passage defines and proves the reality of the balance (mizan) that will be used on the Day of Judgment. It begins by quoting the matn line that 'like this weight and balance, books or entities are weighed.' The commentary explains that this refers to the weighing of the deeds of the servants, and that the balance is a physical instrument (āla ḥissiyya). It emphasizes that belief in this is obligatory based on revelation (samʿī). To support this, it cites three Quranic verses: al-Aʿraf 8, al-Anbiya 47, and al-Muʾminun 102-103, which explicitly mention the weight and scales. Then it gives a linguistic definition of weight (wazn) as the knowledge of a quantity by another in a specified manner. Finally, it states that interpreting the balance literally (ḥaml ʿalā al-ḥaqīqa) is possible, but we do not specify its exact nature. The hadith on this topic are mutawātir (massively transmitted), reason (ʿaql) permits it, and therefore it is a subject of this discipline (kalam), and one must believe in it.

الوزن

خفة

Misconception: The balance is merely metaphorical or represents justice, not a real physical instrument.
Correction: The author affirms it is a real physical instrument (āla ḥissiyya) and belief in it is obligatory based on revelation and reason.

Checkpoint

A) They are ahad (solitary) reports.
B) They have reached the level of tawatur (mass transmission).
C) They are weak (da'if).

Key Takeaway
The balance on the Day of Judgment is a real, physical instrument whose existence is proven by Quran, mutawatir hadith, and reason, and belief in it is obligatory.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Your deeds will be placed on a real balance that you will see with your own eyes. Which of your actions today will tip that scale toward success, and which will make it light? What will you change right now to ensure the heavy side wins?
?
The author insists the balance is not a metaphor—it is a physical reality. Do you live as if your every word and deed is being recorded and weighed? Or do you act as if judgment is distant? What one habit can you start today to increase the weight of your good deeds?
?
If your book of deeds were taken from you and placed on the balance at this moment, would you be confident in the outcome? What specific sin or negligence do you need to repent from today—not tomorrow—to avoid finding your scales light?

Is the Balance One or Multiple?
Discussion of the scholarly views on whether the balance is singular or plural.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the well-known Sunni view is that the balance on the Day of Judgment is one, while an alternative view allows for multiple balances for different deeds.

Core Idea
The plural 'mawazin' in the Quran is for glorification, not for multiplicity.

This lesson examines a classic theological question: Is there one balance or many? The passage presents the majority view that a single balance weighs all deeds for all nations, explaining the Quranic plural as a form of glorification. It also mentions a minority view that each person may have multiple balances for different categories of deeds.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Start by reading the Arabic passage once, then read the English translation. Let the author's argument sink in before analyzing.
Notice the bracketed heading which frames the question.
2
Identify the two opinions
The passage presents two views. Find and note them: the well-known view and the alternative view.
The well-known view is introduced with 'والمشهور'.
3
Understand the linguistic point
The plural 'الموازين' in the verse is explained as being for glorification (للتعظيم). Consider why this is important.
This resolves the apparent conflict between the singular view and the plural Quranic wording.
4
Reflect on the significance
Ask yourself: Why does this distinction matter for Islamic creed? How does it affect our understanding of divine justice?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[هَل الميزانُ واحد أو مُتعدِدُ؟] والمشهور : أَنَّه ميزان واحدٌ لجميع الأمم ولجميع الأعمال (۲)؛ فالجَمْع في قوله تعالى: ﴿وَنَضَعُ الْمَوَازِينَ ﴾ للتَّعظيم، وقيل: يجوز أن يكون للعامل الواحد موازين يوزنُ بكلِّ منها صِنفٌ مِن عَمَلِهِ .
[Is the balance one or multiple?] And the well-known [view] is that it is one balance for all nations and for all deeds (2); so the plural in His statement 'And We shall set up the scales' is for glorification, and it is said: it is permissible that for the individual there are multiple scales, by each of which a type of his deed is weighed.
Source pages p. 537

Commentary
This passage addresses the question of whether the balance (mizan) is one or multiple. It presents the famous (mashhūr) opinion that it is a single balance for all nations and all deeds. The plural form 'al-mawāzīn' in the Quranic verse (al-Anbiya 47) is then explained as being for glorification (li-l-taʿẓīm), not to indicate multiplicity. However, an alternative view is also mentioned: it is possible that for each individual there are multiple balances, each weighing a specific type of deed. Thus, the passage records two opinions, with the first being the more prevalent.

Key Terms
الميزان
الموازين
التعظيم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The plural 'mawazin' in the Quran necessarily implies multiple balances.
Correction: The passage clarifies that the plural is used for glorification and does not contradict the well-known view of a single balance.

Checkpoint

C) There is no balance at all.

Key Takeaway
The famous Sunni position holds that there is one balance for all deeds and nations, and the plural 'mawazin' in the Quranic verse is a form of glorification.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The plural 'mawazin' is for glorification—Allah uses majestic language to emphasize the gravity of the weighing. Does the thought of that one, awe-inspiring scale make you feel more focused on accountability or more anxious? How does that feeling change what you do tomorrow?

Who Is Exempt from the Weighing?
Determination of which beings are subject to the weighing of deeds.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand which beings are exempt from the weighing of deeds on the Day of Judgment and the scriptural and rational basis for their exemption.

Core Idea
Not every soul will be weighed; prophets and angels are exempt from the scales.

This lesson addresses a specific question in eschatology: Who will be subject to the weighing of deeds? The author draws on a prophetic hadith and rational argument to show that the weighing applies only to those who are subject to accounting, thereby exempting prophets and angels.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Begin by reading the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice that the author starts with a question and then gives a ruling with evidence.
2
Identify the groups exempted
The passage mentions three categories: (1) those from the Prophet's ummah who have no account, (2) prophets, and (3) angels. Note the phrase 'وأحرى الأنبياء' which means 'more so the prophets'.
3
Understand the reasoning
The author argues that weighing is a branch (farʿ) of accounting and the recording of deeds. Therefore, those who are not subject to accounting (like the exempted ones) are not weighed. Angels are not weighed because they have no deeds recorded or accounted.
4
Reflect on the implication
Ask yourself: Why does this distinction matter? It emphasizes that the balance is a tool for justice for those who are accountable, not a universal ritual.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[ هَل الميزانُ في حقٌّ كُلّ أَحدٍ ؟] ولا يكون في حقٍّ كلّ أحدٍ ؛ لحديث: يا محمَّد أَدخل الجنَّةَ مِن أُمَّتِك مَن لا حِساب عليه من الباب الأيمن (۳) وأحرى الأنبياء عليهم السَّلام ، وكذا لا يكون للملائكة ؛ لأنَّه فرع عن الحساب وعن كتابة الأعمال ، خصوصاً على القول بأنَّ الصُّحف هي الَّتي تُوضَع في الميزان.
[Is the balance applicable to everyone?] And it is not applicable to everyone; due to the hadith: 'O Muhammad, enter Paradise from your ummah those who have no account from the right door' (3), and more so the prophets (peace be upon them), and likewise it is not for the angels, because it is a branch of the accounting and of the writing of deeds, especially according to the view that the scrolls are what are placed in the balance.
Source pages p. 537

Commentary
This passage addresses whether the weighing on the Day of Judgment applies to every individual. It states that it does not apply to everyone. The evidence is a hadith where the Prophet ﷺ is told that those of his ummah who will be without any reckoning (ḥisāb) will enter Paradise from a special door. This implies that such people are not subject to the weighing. More so (aḥrā) the prophets are exempt. Likewise, the angels are not subject to the weighing because the weighing is a branch (farʿ) of the accounting and the recording of deeds, and the angels are not written deeds as humans are. This is especially true if one holds that the scrolls (ṣuḥuf) are what are placed in the balance. Thus, the passage clarifies that the balance is specifically for those who have deeds recorded and are subject to accounting.

Key Terms
الميزان
الحساب
كتابة الأعمال
الصحف
أحرى الأنبياء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Every individual, including prophets and angels, will undergo the weighing of deeds.
Correction: The passage clarifies that the weighing is not for everyone. Prophets and angels are exempt, as are those who are exempted from accounting.

Checkpoint

A) Sinners from the ummah.
B) The prophets.
C) The believers who have good deeds.
D) The disbelievers.

Key Takeaway
The weighing of deeds is not a universal event; it applies only to those who are accountable, exempting prophets and angels.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Knowing that a group from this ummah will enter Paradise without any account, do you truly live with the hope of being among them, or do you rely on your deeds alone? What would change if you took that promise seriously today?
?
If the prophets—the best of creation—are exempt from the scales, what does that say about your own state? Are you striving for a level of faith where accountability is light, or are you accumulating deeds while neglecting the heart?
?
The angels are not weighed because their worship is constant and without sin. How does this contrast with your own deeds? Will your scrolls be heavy with sincerity or burdened with heedlessness? What one habit can you change right now to align your heart more with the angels' devotion?

The Balance: Literal Reality in Samiyyat
States the literal interpretation and kalam status of the balance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the kalam position on the balance (al-mizan) as a samiyyat matter, including its literal interpretation and the basis for belief in it.

Core Idea
The balance is real and literal, even if its exact substance is unknown.

In this lesson, we examine the balance as a samiyyat issue. The author clarifies that it is a literal real object, not metaphorical, and that its hadiths are reliably transmitted. This establishes it as a valid topic for theological discussion and obligatory belief.

Guided Path
1
Read the source passage
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice the compressed style and the key terms: السمعيات, الميزان, الحقيقة, التواتر.
2
Identify the author's claims

3

This connects to the broader samiyyat methodology.

The hadiths about it are mutawatir (massively transmitted), so certain. Reason does not reject it. Therefore, it is a legitimate subject for kalam. Is the Balance for Everyone? Exemptions from the Mizan
Clarifies exemptions from the balance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the balance (mīzān) does not apply to all creatures; some are exempt based on hadith and rational deduction.

Core Idea
The balance is not for everyone – prophets and angels are exempt.

This lesson examines a commonly misunderstood point: does everyone undergo the weighing of deeds on the Day of Judgment? The author clarifies that the balance is not for everyone. He cites a prophetic hadith and extends the exemption to prophets and angels, grounding his reasoning in the nature of the balance as derived from accounting and written records.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the literal translation. Notice the author's concise style as he presents the hadith and his own deduction.
The hadith is central – understand its implication before moving on.
2
Identify the hadith and its implication
The author cites a hadith about some entering Paradise without account. Consider: who are these people? The author then says prophets are more deserving of exemption.
The phrase 'wa aḥrā al-anbiyā'' shows analogical reasoning.
3
Understand the exclusion of angels
Angels are excluded because the balance is derivative of accounting and written deeds. Especially if one holds that the scrolls (ṣuḥuf) are placed in the balance, angels have no such scrolls.
This is a logical deduction from the nature of the balance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
هَل الميزانُ في حقٌّ كُلّ أَحدٍ؟ ولا يكون في حقٌّ كلّ أحدٍ؛ لحديث: يا محمَّد أَدخل الجنَّةَ مِن أُمَّتِك مَن لا حِساب عليه من الباب الأيمن وأحرى الأنبياء عليهم السَّلام، وكذا لا يكون للملائكة؛ لأنَّه فرع عن الحساب وعن كتابة الأعمال، خصوصاً على القول بأنَّ الصُّحف هي الَّتي تُوضَع في الميزان.

Source pages p. 537

Commentary
This passage answers whether the weighing applies to all creatures. The author says it is not for everyone. He cites a hadith in which the Prophet is told to admit those without account from a specific gate, implying exemption. Prophets are even more exempt. Angels are also excluded because the balance is derived from accounting and recording of deeds, which do not apply to angels. Especially if one holds that the scrolls (suhuf) are placed in the balance, then those without scrolls (like angels) are not weighed.

Weighing the Books of Deeds
Presents the majority view that books of deeds are weighed.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the majority position that the books of deeds are weighed in the balance, along with the evidence from the hadith of the card.

Core Idea
The balance weighs the books of deeds, not the deeds themselves.

Islamic scholars held different views about what exactly is weighed on the Day of Judgment. The dominant position, as the author indicates, is that the books containing each person's good and bad deeds are weighed. This view is supported by a famous hadith about a single card (bitaqah) outweighing many scrolls.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once to get a sense of the language, then read the literal translation. Note the key phrases: 'فتوزن الكتب' and 'حديث البطاقة'.
2
Identify the main claim
The passage states that the books containing deeds are weighed. This is based on the view that good and evil deeds are recorded in separate books.
The author is presenting the majority view.
3
Understand the evidence
The hadith of the card (bitaqah) is cited as evidence. This hadith describes a single card with the declaration of faith outweighing many scrolls of sins.
This hadith supports the idea that written records are weighed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أقوالُ العُلماء في كَيفية الوَزِنِ. ولما اختلف العلماء في الموزُونِ ما هو؟ أشار إليه بقوله: (فَتُوزَنُ الكُتُبُ الَّتي اشتملت على أعمال العباد؛ بناءً على أنَّ الحسنات مُتميّزة بكتاب والسيئات بآخر، ويشهد له حديث البطاقة، وإلى هذا ذهب جمهور.
Scholars' statements on the manner of weighing. And when the scholars differed on what is the weighed thing, he referred to it by his saying: 'So the books that contain the deeds of the servants are weighed, based on the view that good deeds are distinguished by a book and evil deeds by another, and the hadith of the card (bitaqah) testifies to this. And the majority adopted this view.'
Source pages p. 538

Commentary
This passage discusses a disagreement among scholars about what exactly is weighed in the balance. The author quotes the view (attributed to the text of the Jawharah) that the books (kutub) containing the deeds are weighed. This is based on the idea that each person has separate books for good and bad deeds. Evidence is the hadith of the bitaqah (card) where a single card with the shahadah outweighs many scrolls. The majority of scholars adopt this position.

Key Terms
الكتب
البطاقة
الحسنات
السيئات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think deeds themselves are weighed.
Correction: This passage clarifies that it is the books of deeds that are weighed, based on the majority view.

Checkpoint
What evidence does the author cite for the view that books of deeds are weighed?
A) A verse from the Quran.
B) The hadith of the bitaqah (card).
C) Consensus of the Companions.
D) Rational proof.

Key Takeaway
The majority of scholars hold that the books containing deeds are weighed, as evidenced by the hadith of the card.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The hadith of the bitāqah shows that a single sincere declaration of faith can outweigh a lifetime of sins. Is your shahadah alive in your heart today, or is it just a word on your lips? What will you do today to revive its weight in your life?
?
If your book of deeds were opened now, would you be confident that your good deeds are recorded in a separate book, distinct from your sins? What is one sin you need to repent from so that your book becomes lighter?
?
The majority view is that the books themselves are weighed, not each deed separately. Does this make you think about the overall direction of your life rather than isolated actions? What one change can you make this week to shift your books' balance positively?

Weighing the Deeds of Disbelievers
Sanusi clarifies the weighing of disbelievers' evil deeds and explains the verse denying them weight.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the evil deeds of disbelievers (other than disbelief) are weighed on the Day of Judgment for just punishment, and that the Quranic denial of weight refers to beneficial weight.

Core Idea
Even disbelievers' evil deeds are weighed, but only disbelief is excluded.

The scale is a reality of the Day of Judgment, but what about the deeds of disbelievers? A common misconception is that their deeds are not weighed at all. This lesson clarifies that their evil deeds—excluding the sin of disbelief itself—will indeed be weighed for just recompense, while the Quranic verse denying them weight means beneficial weight.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Begin by reading the Arabic and English translation to grasp the author's argument.
2
Understand the clarification on disbelievers
Notice that the author first asks a question and then affirms that weighing is possible for their sins except kufr. Why is kufr excluded? Because it merits eternal punishment without needing a scale.
3
Analyze the Quranic verse
The verse from Al-Kahf is cited. The author interprets 'weight' as beneficial weight. Contrast this with the weighing of their other sins.
4
Reflect on divine justice and grace
Consider how this teaching balances God's justice (punishing evil deeds) and mercy (not weighing disbelief beneficially).
This connects to broader themes of 'adl.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
هَلْ تُوزَنُ أعمالُ الكفارِ؟ ولا مانع من وزن سيّئات الكفّار غير الكفر؛ ليُجَازوا عليها بالعِقاب؛ فقوله تعالى: ﴿فَلَا نُقِيمُ لَهُمْ يَوْمَ الْقِيَمَةِ وَزَنَا﴾ [الكهف: ١٠٥]، أي: نافعاً، وخِفَّة الموزون وثِقَلُه على صورته في الدُّنيا. [أقوالُ العُلماء في كَيفية الوَزِنِ] ولما اختلف العلماء في الموزُونِ ما هو؟ أشار إليه بقوله: (فَتُوزَنُ الكُتُبُ الَّتي اشتملت على أعمال العباد؛ بناءً على أنَّ الحسنات مُتميّزة بكتاب والسيئات بآخر، ويشهد له حديث البطاقة، وإلى هذا ذهب جمهور المفسرين (أو الأَعْيَانُ) يعني: أعيان الأعمال؛ فتُصوّر الأعمال الصالحة بصورة حَسنةٍ نُورانيَّة، ثمَّ تُطرح في كِفَّة النُّور، وهي اليَمينُ المُعدَّةُ للحسنات؛ فتثقل بفضل الله له، وتُصوّر الأعمالُ السَّيِّئَةُ بصُوررة قبيحة ظُلمانيَّة، ثم تُطرح في كِفَّة الظُّلمة، وهي الشِّمال المُعدَّة للسَّيِّئَاتِ؛ فَتَخِفُ بعَدل الله سبحانه.
Are the deeds of the disbelievers weighed? There is no obstacle to weighing the evil deeds of the disbelievers other than disbelief, so that they may be requited for them with punishment. Thus His statement, the Exalted: {So We shall not assign to them on the Day of Resurrection any weight} [Al-Kahf: 105], meaning beneficial weight. The lightness or heaviness of the weighed object is according to its form in this world. [Sayings of the scholars on the manner of weighing] And when the scholars differed as to what is weighed, he [the author] alluded to it with his saying: (So the books that contained the deeds of the servants are weighed, based on the fact that good deeds are distinguished by one book and evil deeds by another, and the hadith of the card (al-bitaqa) attests to this; and this is the view of the majority of the exegetes. (Or the deeds themselves (al-aʿyān)) meaning the individual deeds themselves; so righteous deeds are pictured in a beautiful, luminous form, then cast into the pan of light, which is the right side prepared for good deeds, thus they become heavy by God's grace for him, and evil deeds are pictured in an ugly, dark form, then cast into the pan of darkness, which is the left side prepared for evil deeds, thus they become light by the justice of God, the Exalted.)
Source pages p. 538

Commentary
This passage addresses the question of whether the deeds of disbelievers will be weighed on the Day of Judgment. The author first clarifies that there is no problem in weighing their evil deeds (excluding disbelief itself, which deserves eternal punishment without need for weighing) so that they may receive proportionate punishment. He then cites the Quranic verse from Al-Kahf 105, explaining that the 'weight' denied to disbelievers is beneficial weight; their deeds may still be weighed but to no avail. The discussion then moves to differing scholarly opinions on the exact object of weighing. The author presents two main views. First, the view of the majority of exegetes: that the actual written records (books) containing the deeds of the servants are weighed. This is supported by the hadith of the card (al-bitaqa), which describes a man's scrolls being outweighed by a card containing the testimony of faith. Second, the alternative view (indicated by 'or the deeds themselves'): that it is the deeds themselves—their very substances—that are weighed. In this view, good deeds are embodied as beautiful, luminous forms placed in the right pan (prepared for good deeds), becoming heavy by God's grace. Evil deeds are embodied as ugly, dark forms placed in the left pan, becoming light (i.e., insignificant) by God's justice. The passage thus explains the theological reality of the scale, balancing divine grace and justice.

Key Terms
وزن
أعمال الكفار

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think disbelievers' deeds are not weighed at all.
Correction: The passage clarifies that their evil deeds (except disbelief) are weighed for just punishment, but they do not receive beneficial weight.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why are the evil deeds of disbelievers (other than disbelief) weighed?
A) To grant them reward
B) To requite them with punishment
C) To increase their rank
D) To be thrown away

Key Takeaway
Disbelievers' evil deeds are weighed for just punishment, but the Quranic denial of weight means beneficial weight, not absolute non-weighing.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If disbelief nullifies every good deed, then what hidden doubts or moments of disbelief have you allowed into your heart this week? Are you certain that your faith is pure enough for your deeds to have weight?
?
The verse says disbelievers will have no beneficial weight. Your deeds will be weighed too. Which of your deeds do you fear will be light? What are you doing today to increase their weight?
?
The author says that evil deeds are weighed for punishment. When you look at your own sins, do you truly feel the terror of that weighing? Or do you take lightly the deeds that will be placed on the scale against you?

The Object of Weighing: Books or Embodied Deeds?
Sanusi presents two scholarly views on what exactly is weighed on the scale.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two main scholarly opinions on what is placed on the scale on the Day of Judgment: the written records of deeds or the deeds themselves in embodied form.

Core Idea
Scholars differ: is it the books of deeds or the deeds themselves that are weighed?

After establishing that deeds are weighed, scholars debated the exact nature of what is placed on the scale. Is it the physical books containing the record of each person’s deeds, or is it the deeds themselves transformed into luminous or dark forms? This lesson presents both views, along with the evidence for each.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic and translation to see the two opinions presented by the author.
2
Identify the first opinion
The author says 'the books that contained the deeds are weighed' based on the hadith of the card. This is the view of the majority of exegetes.
3
Identify the second opinion
The alternative view (indicated by 'or the deeds themselves') holds that the deeds themselves are embodied as forms, good deeds as luminous and evil deeds as dark, and then placed in respective pans.
4
Compare the two views
Notice the difference: the first opinion focuses on a written record, the second on the substance of the deed. Both rely on the notion of representation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
هَلْ تُوزَنُ أعمالُ الكفارِ؟ ولا مانع من وزن سيّئات الكفّار غير الكفر؛ ليُجَازوا عليها بالعِقاب؛ فقوله تعالى: ﴿فَلَا نُقِيمُ لَهُمْ يَوْمَ الْقِيَمَةِ وَزَنَا﴾ [الكهف: ١٠٥]، أي: نافعاً، وخِفَّة الموزون وثِقَلُه على صورته في الدُّنيا. [أقوالُ العُلماء في كَيفية الوَزِنِ] ولما اختلف العلماء في الموزُونِ ما هو؟ أشار إليه بقوله: (فَتُوزَنُ الكُتُبُ الَّتي اشتملت على أعمال العباد؛ بناءً على أنَّ الحسنات مُتميّزة بكتاب والسيئات بآخر، ويشهد له حديث البطاقة، وإلى هذا ذهب جمهور المفسرين (أو الأَعْيَانُ) يعني: أعيان الأعمال؛ فتُصوّر الأعمال الصالحة بصورة حَسنةٍ نُورانيَّة، ثمَّ تُطرح في كِفَّة النُّور، وهي اليَمينُ المُعدَّةُ للحسنات؛ فتثقل بفضل الله له، وتُصوّر الأعمالُ السَّيِّئَةُ بصُوررة قبيحة ظُلمانيَّة، ثم تُطرح في كِفَّة الظُّلمة، وهي الشِّمال المُعدَّة للسَّيِّئَاتِ؛ فَتَخِفُ بعَدل الله سبحانه.
Are the deeds of the disbelievers weighed? There is no obstacle to weighing the evil deeds of the disbelievers other than disbelief, so that they may be requited for them with punishment. Thus His statement, the Exalted: {So We shall not assign to them on the Day of Resurrection any weight} [Al-Kahf: 105], meaning beneficial weight. The lightness or heaviness of the weighed object is according to its form in this world. [Sayings of the scholars on the manner of weighing] And when the scholars differed as to what is weighed, he [the author] alluded to it with his saying: (So the books that contained the deeds of the servants are weighed, based on the fact that good deeds are distinguished by one book and evil deeds by another, and the hadith of the card (al-bitaqa) attests to this; and this is the view of the majority of the exegetes. (Or the deeds themselves (al-aʿyān)) meaning the individual deeds themselves; so righteous deeds are pictured in a beautiful, luminous form, then cast into the pan of light, which is the right side prepared for good deeds, thus they become heavy by God's grace for him, and evil deeds are pictured in an ugly, dark form, then cast into the pan of darkness, which is the left side prepared for evil deeds, thus they become light by the justice of God, the Exalted.)

Commentary
This passage addresses the question of whether the deeds of disbelievers will be weighed on the Day of Judgment. The author first clarifies that there is no problem in weighing their evil deeds (excluding disbelief itself, which deserves eternal punishment without need for weighing) so that they may receive proportionate punishment. The discussion then moves to differing scholarly opinions on the exact object of weighing. The author presents two main views. First, the view of the majority of exegetes: that the actual written records (books) containing the deeds of the servants are weighed. This is supported by the hadith of the card (al-bitaqa), which describes a man's scrolls being outweighed by a card containing the testimony of faith. Second, the alternative view (indicated by 'or the deeds themselves'): that it is the deeds themselves—their very substances—that are weighed. Evil deeds are embodied as ugly, dark forms placed in the left pan, becoming light (i.e., insignificant) by God's justice. The passage thus explains the theological reality of the scale, balancing divine grace and justice.

?

How Deeds Are Weighed on the Day of Judgment
The commentator explains the transformation of deeds into physical forms and their weighing.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how good and evil deeds are transformed into physical forms and weighed in the balance by God's grace and justice.

Core Idea
Deeds become luminous or dark bodies; their weight determines divine reward or punishment.

This passage from the commentary on Jawharat al-Tawhid explains one of the eschatological events: the weighing of deeds. The author describes how each deed is given a tangible form corresponding to its nature—beautiful for good, ugly for evil—and then placed in the appropriate pan of the balance. This is not merely metaphorical but a real transformation that may involve a breach of natural custom.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Let the description of the transformation and the weighing settle in.
2
Identify the two categories of deeds
Notice that good deeds are pictured as luminous forms and placed in the right pan, while evil deeds are dark forms placed in the left pan.
The right pan is for good deeds, the left for evil deeds.
3
Understand the role of grace and justice
Observe that good deeds become heavy by God's grace, while evil deeds become light by God's justice.
The commentary clarifies that lightness of evil deeds is by justice, not grace.
4
Reflect on the two opinions about transformation
The passage mentions two views: either the true nature of the deeds is transformed, or God creates entirely new bodies corresponding to the deeds.
Both are possible as a breach of custom.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قسم السمعيات
المفسرين (۱) (أو الأَعْيَانُ) يعني: أعيان الأعمال؛ فتُصوّر الأعمال الصالحة بصورة حسنةٍ نُورانيَّة، ثمَّ تُطرح في كِفَّة النُّور، وهي اليَمينُ المُعدَّةُ للحسنات؛ فتثقل بفضل الله له، وتُصوّر الأعمالُ السَّيِّئَةُ بصورة قبيحة ظُلمانيَّة، ثم تُطرح في كِفَّة الظُّلمة، وهي الشِّمال المُعدَّة للسَّيِّئَاتِ؛ فَتَخِفُ بعَدل الله سبحانه (۲)،
وهو عند ابن المبارك في زوائد الزهد (۳۷۱) وفيه يستخص بدل: يستخلص وأخرجه الترمذي (٢٦٣٩) عن سويد بن نصر، وابن حبان (٢٢٥) من طريق عبد الوارث بن عبيد الله، والبغوي (٤٣٢١) من طريق إبراهيم بن عبد الله الخلال، ثلاثتهم عن ابن المبارك، بهذا الإسناد قال الترمذي: هذا حديث حسن غريب. وأخرجه ابن ماجه (٤٣٠٠) من طريق ابن أبي مريم والحاكم ٦/١، وعنه البيهقي في الشعب (۲۸۳) من طريق يونس بن محمد (وهو المؤدب) و ٥٢٩/١ من طريق يحيى بن عبد الله بن بكير، ثلاثتهم عن الليث بن سعد، وصححه الحاكم في الموضع الأول على شرط مسلم، ووافقه الذهبي، وقال في الموضع الثاني: صحيح الإسناد، ولم يخرجاه، ووافقه الذهبي. وقوله في أول الحديث: "إن الله يستخلص" جاء في مصادر التخريج: "سيخلص"، وجاء عند ابن ماجه والحاكم ٥٢٩/١: يُصاح برجل من أمتي وقوله في آخر الحديث: "ولا يثقل شيء بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم" هكذا ورد في الأصول التي بأيدينا، وجاء عند ابن المبارك وابن حبان: "لا يثقل اسم الله شيء" وجاء عند غيرهما: "لا يثقل مع اسم الله شيء" فيظهر أن ما جاء في أصول المسند زيادة من النساخ.
قوله: (يستخلص رجلا) أي يخرجه من بينهم ويميزه عنهم ويظهره. قاله السندي.
قوله: (سجلا) بالكسر والتشديد هو الكتاب الكبير.
قوله: (فبهت الرجل) البهت الانقطاع والحيرة. والبطاقة رقعة صغيرة. قاله ابن الأثير.
قوله: (فطاشت السجلات) أي: خفت.
(۱) قيل: وقد يوزن الشخص نفسه؛ لحديث ابن مسعود: "رجله في الميزان أثقل من جبل أحد". الأمير. والحديث عند أبي نعيم في الحلية (١٧٥/١)
(۲) قوله: (فتخف) وهذا ليس لكل عبد، بل عبد أراد الله به خيرا. الشنواني. وقوله: (بعدل الله بل بالفضل، إنما المُناسب للعدل ثقل السيئات. الأمير.
ولا يمتنع قلب الحقائق خَرْقًا للعادة (۱) ، وقيل : يخلق الله تعالى أجساما على عدد تلك الأعمال من غير قَلْبٍ لها .
ومن فوائد الوَزْنِ: امتحانُ العِباد بالإيمان بالغيب في الدُّنيا، وجعل ذلك علامة لأهل السَّعادة والشَّقاوة، وتعريفُ العِباد ما لهم من الجزاء على الخير والشَّرِّ ، وإقامة الحجة عليهم.
(۱) قوله: (خرقا للعادة) أي: لأن المُستحيل العقلي القلب مع آثار الأولى، كما في شرح المصنف للتناقض ، وقد أوضحنا المقام عند قوله : فقدرة بمكن تعلقت . الأمير .
Section of matters heard (by revelation). The interpreters (1) (or the essences) means: the essences of deeds; so good deeds are pictured in a beautiful luminous form, then they are thrown into the pan of light, which is the right side prepared for good deeds; so they become heavy by the grace of God for him, and evil deeds are pictured in an ugly dark form, then they are thrown into the pan of darkness, which is the left side prepared for evil deeds; so they become light by the justice of God (2). And it is with Ibn al-Mubarak in Zawa'id al-Zuhd (371) and in it 'yastakhiss' instead of 'yastakhlish'. And it was narrated by al-Tirmidhi (2639) from Suwayd ibn Nasr, and Ibn Hibban (225) via Abd al-Warith ibn Ubayd Allah, and al-Baghawi (4321) via Ibrahim ibn Abd Allah al-Khallal, all three from Ibn al-Mubarak with this chain. Al-Tirmidhi said: this hadith is hasan gharib. And it was narrated by Ibn Majah (4300) via Ibn Abi Maryam and al-Hakim 6/1, and from him by al-Bayhaqi in al-Shu'ab (283) via Yunus ibn Muhammad (who is al-Mu'adhdhib) and 529/1 via Yahya ibn Abd Allah ibn Bukayr, all three from al-Layth ibn Sa'd. Al-Hakim authenticated it in the first place on the condition of Muslim, and al-Dhahabi agreed, and he said in the second place: sound chain, and they did not include it, and al-Dhahabi agreed. And his saying at the beginning of the hadith: 'Indeed God will extract' came in the sources of extraction: 'will give success', and it came with Ibn Majah and al-Hakim 529/1: 'a man from my ummah will be called' and his saying at the end of the hadith: 'And nothing will weigh heavy with the name of God, the Most Merciful, the Most Compassionate' is how it is reported in the copies we have, and it came with Ibn al-Mubarak and Ibn Hibban: 'Nothing will weigh heavy the name of God' and it came with others: 'Nothing will weigh heavy with the name of God'. So it appears that what came in the copies of al-Musnad is an addition by the copyists. His saying: (He extracts a man) means He takes him out from among them and distinguishes him from them and makes him appear. Al-Sindi said it. His saying: (a sijill) with kasra and shadda is the large book. His saying: (the man became bewildered) al-bahat is confusion and perplexity. And al-bitaqa is a small card. Ibn al-Athir said it. His saying: (the registers flew away) means they became light. (1) It is said: And the person himself may be weighed, according to the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud: 'His foot in the balance is heavier than Mount Uhud.' Al-Amir. And the hadith is with Abu Nu'aym in al-Hilya (175/1). (2) His saying: (so it becomes light) and this is not for every servant, but for a servant whom God intends good. Al-Shanwani. And his saying: (by the justice of God but rather by grace, only the weight of evil deeds is appropriate for justice. Al-Amir. And it is not impossible to transform the true nature of things as a breach of custom (1), and it is said: God creates bodies in the number of those deeds without transformation. And among the benefits of the weighing: testing the servants by belief in the unseen in the world, and making that a sign for the people of happiness and misery, and informing the servants what they have of recompense for good and evil, and establishing the proof against them. (1) His saying: (as a breach of custom) meaning: because the intellectual impossibility is the transformation while preserving the original traces, as in the explanation of the author about contradiction, and we have clarified the matter at his saying: 'For power is possible to have been attached.' Al-Amir.
Source pages p. 539

Commentary
This passage covers the doctrine of weighing deeds (al-wazn) in the balance on the Day of Judgment. It begins by explaining that deeds are transformed into bodies: good deeds into a beautiful luminous form placed in the right pan (the scale of light), and evil deeds into an ugly dark form placed in the left pan (the scale of darkness). The good deeds weigh heavy by God's grace, while evil deeds weigh light by God's justice. Then the text provides hadith verification for this concept, citing multiple chains. It also clarifies lexical meanings of key terms in the hadith like 'yastakhlish' (to extract), 'sijill' (large book), 'bahita' (confused), 'bitaqa' (small card), and 'tāsha' (become light). Then it addresses a question: can the person himself be weighed? It cites a hadith that a person's foot may be heavier than Mount Uhud. Another note clarifies that the weighing applies only to the servant whom God intends good. Then the passage continues with the philosophical point that it is not impossible for God to transform the true nature of things as a miracle, and a second opinion holds that God creates bodies equal to the number of deeds without transformation. Finally, the benefits of the weighing are enumerated: testing servants by belief in the unseen, making it a sign of happiness or misery, informing them of their recompense, and establishing the proof against them.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the weighing is only metaphorical, not a real physical transformation of deeds.
Correction: The passage affirms that deeds are literally transformed into luminous or dark forms and weighed in a real balance.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what causes good deeds to become heavy in the balance?
A) Their own intrinsic merit
B) God's grace (فضل)
C) The angel's hand

Key Takeaway

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you consider that your deeds will be turned into luminous or dark bodies and weighed, what specific action from your past week would you most fear to see in the pan of darkness? What will you do today to turn that deed into light?
?
The lesson states that good deeds become heavy by God’s grace, not by your own merit. Does this truth humble you or make you complacent? How will you respond to God’s grace this week in a tangible way?
?
If the weight of your evil deeds is lightened only by God’s justice, are you banking on that justice as a mere formality, or are you actively seeking His mercy to tip the scale? What one change will you make starting tonight to ensure your right pan outweighs the left?

The Benefits of the Weighing of Deeds
The commentator enumerates the benefits of the weighing of deeds.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the four benefits of the weighing of deeds on the Day of Judgment.

Core Idea
The weighing tests belief in the unseen, marks happiness or misery, informs recompense, and establishes proof.

After explaining the mechanics of the weighing, the commentator lists several divine wisdoms behind this event. These benefits highlight why the weighing is not only a physical process but also a means of spiritual testing and justice. This passage connects the eschatological event to the purposes of divine wisdom.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once to get the list of benefits. Notice the concise wording.
2
Identify each benefit
There are four benefits explicitly mentioned. Find them and understand what each one means.
They are: testing belief in the unseen, making it a sign, informing recompense, and establishing proof.
3
Consider the significance of each benefit
Reflect on how each benefit relates to God's justice and mercy, and to the purpose of the Day of Judgment.
4
Think about the connection to belief in the unseen
The first benefit emphasizes that the weighing requires faith in the unseen in this world, which is a test.

ومن فوائد الوَزْنِ: امتحانُ العِباد بالإيمان بالغيب في الدُّنيا، وجعل ذلك علامة لأهل السَّعادة والشَّقاوة، وتعريفُ العِباد ما لهم من الجزاء على الخير والشَّرِّ ، وإقامة الحجة عليهم.

Section of matters heard (by revelation). The interpreters (1) (or the essences) means: the essences of deeds; so good deeds are pictured in a beautiful luminous form, then they are thrown into the pan of light, which is the right side prepared for good deeds; so they become heavy by the grace of God for him, and evil deeds are pictured in an ugly dark form, then they are thrown into the pan of darkness, which is the left side prepared for evil deeds; so they become light by the justice of God (2). And it is with Ibn al-Mubarak in Zawa'id al-Zuhd (371) and in it 'yastakhiss' instead of 'yastakhlish'. And it was narrated by al-Tirmidhi (2639) from Suwayd ibn Nasr, and Ibn Hibban (225) via Abd al-Warith ibn Ubayd Allah, and al-Baghawi (4321) via Ibrahim ibn Abd Allah al-Khallal, all three from Ibn al-Mubarak with this chain. Al-Tirmidhi said: this hadith is hasan gharib. And it was narrated by Ibn Majah (4300) via Ibn Abi Maryam and al-Hakim 6/1, and from him by al-Bayhaqi in al-Shu'ab (283) via Yunus ibn Muhammad (who is al-Mu'adhdhib) and 529/1 via Yahya ibn Abd Allah ibn Bukayr, all three from al-Layth ibn Sa'd. Al-Hakim authenticated it in the first place on the condition of Muslim, and al-Dhahabi agreed, and he said in the second place: sound chain, and they did not include it, and al-Dhahabi agreed. And his saying at the beginning of the hadith: 'Indeed God will extract' came in the sources of extraction: 'will give success', and it came with Ibn Majah and al-Hakim 529/1: 'a man from my ummah will be called' and his saying at the end of the hadith: 'And nothing will weigh heavy with the name of God, the Most Merciful, the Most Compassionate' is how it is reported in the copies we have, and it came with Ibn al-Mubarak and Ibn Hibban: 'Nothing will weigh heavy the name of God' and it came with others: 'Nothing will weigh heavy with the name of God'. So it appears that what came in the copies of al-Musnad is an addition by the copyists. His saying: (He extracts a man) means He takes him out from among them and distinguishes him from them and makes him appear. Al-Sindi said it. His saying: (a sijill) with kasra and shadda is the large book. His saying: (the man became bewildered) al-bahat is confusion and perplexity. And al-bitaqa is a small card. Ibn al-Athir said it. His saying: (the registers flew away) means they became light. (1) It is said: And the person himself may be weighed, according to the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud: 'His foot in the balance is heavier than Mount Uhud.' Al-Amir. And the hadith is with Abu Nu'aym in al-Hilya (175/1). (2) His saying: (so it becomes light) and this is not for every servant, but for a servant whom God intends good. Al-Shanwani. And his saying: (by the justice of God but rather by grace, only the weight of evil deeds is appropriate for justice. Al-Amir. And it is not impossible to transform the true nature of things as a breach of custom (1), and it is said: God creates bodies in the number of those deeds without transformation. And among the benefits of the weighing: testing the servants by belief in the unseen in the world, and making that a sign for the people of happiness and misery, and informing the servants what they have of recompense for good and evil, and establishing the proof against them. (1) His saying: (as a breach of custom) meaning: because the intellectual impossibility is the transformation while preserving the original traces, as in the explanation of the author about contradiction, and we have clarified the matter at his saying: 'For power is possible to have been attached.' Al-Amir.
Source pages p. 539

Commentary
This passage covers the doctrine of weighing deeds (al-wazn) in the balance on the Day of Judgment. It begins by explaining that deeds are transformed into bodies: good deeds into a beautiful luminous form placed in the right pan (the scale of light), and evil deeds into an ugly dark form placed in the left pan (the scale of darkness). The good deeds weigh heavy by God's grace, while evil deeds weigh light by God's justice. Then the text provides hadith verification for this concept, citing multiple chains. It also clarifies lexical meanings of key terms in the hadith like 'yastakhlish' (to extract), 'sijill' (large book), 'bahita' (confused), 'bitaqa' (small card), and 'tāsha' (become light). Then it addresses a question: can the person himself be weighed? It cites a hadith that a person's foot may be heavier than Mount Uhud. Another note clarifies that the weighing applies only to the servant whom God intends good. Then the passage continues with the philosophical point that it is not impossible for God to transform the true nature of things as a miracle, and a second opinion holds that God creates bodies equal to the number of deeds without transformation. Finally, the benefits of the weighing are enumerated: testing servants by belief in the unseen, making it a sign of happiness or misery, informing them of their recompense, and establishing the proof against them.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think the weighing is only about physical weight and not about spiritual purposes.
Correction: The passage clearly enumerates spiritual benefits: testing, sign, recompense, and proof.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The weighing will reveal your recompense for both good and evil. If you were to see your own scale right now, would you be satisfied or terrified? What is the one hidden sin you keep doing that you know will bring misery? Will you abandon it now, before it is too late?
?
You are being tested in this world to believe in a reality you cannot see: the balance. Are you passing that test? Or do you live as if only what you can see matters? How will you change your actions today to prove that you truly believe in the Day of Weighing?

The Sirat and the Crossing of Servants
The commentator defines the Sirat and explains the varying crossing conditions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definition and linguistic roots of the Sirat, the conditions of its crossing, and the scholarly dispute regarding its description.

Core Idea
The Sirat is the bridge over Hell that all must cross, finer than a hair and sharper than a sword.

This passage from the commentary on Jawharat al-Tawhid explains one of the major eschatological signs: the Sirat. It establishes that belief in the Sirat is a matter of revelation (sam'), just like the books and the scale. The commentator defines it linguistically and legally, describes its location and characteristics, and notes that the servants cross it in different states. He also highlights a scholarly disagreement over the literal meaning of its description.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Begin by reading the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the two main sections: the definition of the Sirat and the description of the crossing. Also note the footnotes that elaborate on the linguistic root and the scholarly dispute.
The passage includes a verse from the poem and the commentator's explanation.
2
Understand the linguistic and technical definitions
Focus on the phrase 'والصراط لغة: الطريق الواضح' and 'شرعاً: جسر ممدود على متن جهنم'. The term 'صراط' in Arabic means a clear road, and it is called so because it 'swallows' those who pass. Technically, it is a bridge stretched over Hell, leading to Paradise.
The root 'صرط' implies swallowing, which links to the idea of the bridge devouring those who fall.
3
Examine the crossing conditions and the dispute
Observe that the crossing varies: some are safe, some are torn apart. Then read the footnote (4) about the dispute. The mainstream view takes the description literally, while some scholars interpret it metaphorically as the severity of the crossing.
This dispute is important because it touches on how to interpret hadith descriptions of the afterlife.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مرور العباد على الصراط]
١٠٦- كَذَا الصِّرَاطُ فالعِبَادُ مُخْتلِفٌ مُرورُهُمْ ، فَسَالمٌ وَمُنْتَلِفْ
وجوب
28
(كَذَا الصِّرَاط) يعني: أَنَّه كَأَخْذِ العِبادِ الكُتب وكالوزن والمِيزَان في الإيمان به سمعاً، والصِّرَاط لغة: الطَّريق الواضح، لأنَّه يبتلع المارَّة (۲)، وشرعاً: جِسرٌ ممدود على متن جهنم، يَرِدُه الأَوَّلُون والآخِرون(۳) ذاهبين إلى الجنَّة؛ لأنَّ جهنّم بين الموقف والجنَّة، أدقُ مِن الشَّعر وأَحدُّ مِن السَّيف(٤)،
(۲) قوله: (لأنه يبتلع المارة) أي يصيرون في جوفه، من صرطه يصرطه إذا ابتلعه. الشنواني.
(۳) قوله: (يرده الأولون والآخرون) أي حتى الأنبياء ومَن يدخل بغير حساب، الإنس وغيرهم، وكلهم سكوت إلا الأنبياء وقولهم إذ ذاك: اللهم سلم سلم كذا في الصحيح. الأمير والشنواني.
(٤) هذه مسألة خلافية بين أهل السنة، والمشهور قولهم بأنه أدق من الشعرة وأَحدُّ مِن السيف، وخالف في ذلك العز بن عبد السلام والقرافي وبدر الدين الزركشي، وغيرهم حيث قالوا: على فرض صحة هذه الروايات فهي محمولة على غير المعنى الظاهر، بأن تؤول مثلا بالشدة والمشَقَّة الحاصلة عند عبور الجسر، وعندها فلا يُنافي ما ورد من الأحاديث الدالة على قيام الملائكة على جنبيه، وكون الكلاليب فيه.
The passage of the servants over the Sirat. 106- Likewise the Sirat: the servants are different in their crossing, so some are safe and some are torn apart. Necessary? 28. (Likewise the Sirat) means: that it is like the taking of the books and the weighing and the balance in believing in it by revelation. And the Sirat linguistically: the clear road, because it swallows the passersby (2). And legally: a bridge stretched over the surface of Hell, which the first and the last come to (3) going to Paradise, because Hell is between the standing place and Paradise, finer than a hair and sharper than a sword (4). (2) His saying: (because it swallows the passersby) means they become in its belly, from saratahu yasrutuhu if he swallowed it. Al-Shanwani. (3) His saying: (the first and the last come to it) means even the prophets and those who enter without reckoning, humans and others, and all are silent except the prophets and their saying at that moment: 'O Allah, grant safety, grant safety' as in the authentic. Al-Amir and Al-Shanwani. (4) This is a point of dispute among the Ahl al-Sunnah. Their famous statement is that it is finer than a hair and sharper than a sword. Al-Aziz ibn Abd al-Salam, al-Qarafi, and Badr al-Din al-Zarkashi, and others differed in that, where they said: on the assumption of the authenticity of these narrations, they are interpreted in other than the apparent meaning, for example by interpreting it as the severity and hardship that occurs when crossing the bridge, and in that case it does not contradict what is reported in hadiths that indicate the angels standing on its sides and that there are hooks in it.
Source pages p. 540

Commentary
This passage discusses the second eschatological element: the Sirat, which is a matter of revelation (sam') like the books and the scale. It begins with a verse from the poem stating that servants cross differently—some safe, some torn apart. The commentary explains that the Sirat linguistically means a clear road, and it is called that because it swallows those who pass over it. Technically, it is a bridge stretched over the surface of Hell, coming from hellfire, which all people from first to last must cross on their way to Paradise, since Hell lies between the standing place (al-mawqif) and Paradise. It is described as finer than a hair and sharper than a sword. Then three footnotes elaborate: (2) gives the root meaning of 'yabtali' as swallowing; (3) confirms that even prophets will cross but will be silent except for their plea 'O Allah, grant safety'; and (4) notes a scholarly dispute: the mainstream Ash'ari position takes the description literally, but some prominent scholars (al-'Izz ibn Abd al-Salam, al-Qarafi, al-Zarkashi) interpret it metaphorically as the severity and hardship of the crossing, to avoid contradicting hadiths about angels standing on both sides and hooks attached to the bridge.

أحد من السيف
ابتلاع

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some people think the description of the Sirat as 'finer than a hair and sharper than a sword' is merely metaphorical or hyperbolic, not a real physical bridge.
Correction: The mainstream Ash'ari position holds that the Sirat is a real physical object created by Allah, though its exact nature is beyond human comparison. The description indicates its extreme sharpness and narrowness.

Key Takeaway
