How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The Sirat is described as finer than a hair and sharper than a sword. If you truly believed you would walk across such a bridge tomorrow, what would you do right now to prepare? Is your current lifestyle reflecting that urgency?
?
You know that some scholars interpreted the description metaphorically as extreme difficulty. But the majority affirm it as literal. Which view makes you more fearful of the crossing? And how can that fear translate into a concrete commitment to obedience starting today?

The Sirat: Definition, Nature, and Varying Views
Al-Azhari defines the Sirat and explains its nature and differing views.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the reality of the Sirat (bridge), its linguistic and legal definition, the benefits of the weighing of deeds, and the concept of changing realities as a breaking of custom.

Core Idea
The Sirat is a real bridge over Hell, affirmed by revelation, and the weighing of deeds has profound purposes.

In this lesson, we explore the Sunni doctrine of the Sirat (bridge) as a real, physical bridge over Hell that all must cross. The passage also discusses the divine wisdom behind the weighing of deeds and the possibility of Allah changing realities. Let us dive into the text.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the repetition of 'مرور العباد على الصراط' as a heading.
2
Identify the definition of Sirat
Look for the linguistic and legal definitions of Sirat. Note that the linguistic definition mentions 'the clear path' and the legal definition emphasizes a bridge over Hell.
The legal definition is the key: a bridge over Hell, thinner than a hair and sharper than a sword.
3
List the benefits of the weighing
Find the four benefits of al-wazn (weighing) mentioned in the passage. Write them down.
These benefits include testing belief in the unseen, marking happiness or misery, informing of recompense, and establishing proof.
4
Reflect on changing realities
Consider the statement that 'it is not impossible to change realities as a breaking of custom'. Reflect on what this means for the nature of the Sirat and the transformation of deeds.
This relates to Allah's power to alter physical realities.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مرور العباد على الصراط
ولا يمتنع قلب الحقائق خَرْقًا للعادة، وقيل: يخلق الله تعالى أجساما على عدد تلك الأعمال من غير قَلْبٍ لها.
ومن فوائد الوَزْنِ: امتحانُ العِباد بالإيمان بالغيب في الدُّنيا، وجعل ذلك علامة لأهل السَّعادة والشَّقاوة، وتعريفُ العِباد ما لهم من الجزاء على الخير والشَّرِّ، وإقامة الحجة عليهم.
مرور العباد على الصراط]
١٠٦- كَذَا الصِّرَاطُ فالعِبَادُ مُخْتلِفٌ مُرورُهُمْ، فَسَالمٌ وَمُنْتَلِفْ
(كَذَا الصِّرَاط) يعني: أَنَّه كَأَخْذِ العِبادِ الكُتب وكالوزن والمِيزَان في الإيمان به سمعاً، والصِّرَاط لغة: الطَّريق الواضح، لأنَّه يبتلع المارَّة، وشرعاً: جِسرٌ ممدود على متن جهنم، يَرِدُه الأَوَّلُون والآخِرون ذاهبين إلى الجنَّة؛ لأنَّ جهنّم بين الموقف والجنَّة، أدقُ مِن الشَّعر وأَحدُّ مِن السَّيف.
The passage of the servants over the Sirat. And it is not impossible to change realities as a breaking of custom. And it is said: Allah creates bodies corresponding to the number of those deeds without changing them. And among the benefits of the weighing are: testing the servants by belief in the unseen in this world, making that a sign for the people of happiness and misery, informing the servants of what they have of recompense for good and evil, and establishing the proof against them. The passage of the servants over the Sirat. 106- Likewise the Sirat: the servants' passing over it differs, so one is safe and one is plucked. (Likewise the Sirat) meaning: that it is like the taking of the books and the weighing and the balance in believing in it by transmission. It is thinner than a hair and sharper than a sword.
Source pages p. 540

Commentary
This passage defines the Sirat (bridge) and describes its nature. It begins by stating that the passage of the servants over the Sirat is a real event. Then it addresses the possibility of changing realities as a breaking of custom, meaning that Allah can transform deeds into physical forms if He wills, though some scholars say He creates separate bodies. Then it mentions the benefits of the weighing (al-wazn) that will take place, which are: testing faith in the unseen, distinguishing the blessed from the wretched, and establishing proof. The matn verse "كَذَا الصِّرَاطُ فالعِبَادُ مُخْتلِفٌ مُرورُهُمْ" is then explained: belief in the Sirat is by divine revelation (sam') just like the taking of books and the weighing. The term 'Sirat' is defined linguistically as a clear path, and legally as a bridge over Hell that all people must cross to reach Paradise. It is described as thinner than a hair and sharper than a sword, indicating extreme difficulty. The passage conveys the Sunni view that the Sirat is a real, physical bridge, though there is a footnote disagreement among some scholars about its literal thinness.

Key Terms
الصراط
قلب الحقائق
خرق العادة
الوزن
السمعيات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Sirat is merely a metaphorical representation of the straight path.
Correction: The passage affirms the Sirat as a literal, physical bridge over Hell, thinner than a hair and sharper than a sword, which all must cross.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the legal (shar'an) definition of the Sirat?
A) A clear path in this world
B) A bridge stretched over the surface of Hell
C) A metaphor for the straight path of Islam
D) A weighing scale for deeds

Key Takeaway
The Sirat is a real bridge over Hell, belief in it is by revelation, and the weighing of deeds serves multiple divine purposes.

?

?

The Obligatory Belief in the Sirat
Al-Azhari states the Sunni view and gives the proof for obligation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Sunni position on the Sirat (literal meaning with tafwid) and the evidence that makes belief in it obligatory.

Core Idea
The Sirat is a possible reality affirmed by scripture; belief in it is wajib.

Faith in the unseen includes accepting the Sirat as a true event, not a metaphor. Al-Azhari clarifies that Ahl al-Sunna keep the textual descriptions as they are while delegating their true nature to Allah. This lesson presents the proof for why every Muslim must believe in the Sirat.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Sunni position
Read how Ahl al-Sunna affirm the literal meaning of the Sirat and delegate its true reality to Allah (tafwid). This is the first key idea.
Contrast with the Mu'tazila who interpret the Sirat metaphorically.
2
See the refutation of Mu'tazila
Notice that the passage directly opposes the Mu'tazilite view. The Sunni position is distinct.
3
Grasp the evidence for obligation
The proof is that the Sirat is a possible matter (mumkin) mentioned in the Quran and Sunnah, and agreed upon by consensus. This makes belief obligatory.
Reflect: how does the author use these sources to show the obligation?
4
Connect to kalam methodology
Understand that obligatory belief can originate from revealed sources, not just reason, when the matter is possible.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومذهب أهل السُّنَّة: إبقاؤه على ظاهره، مع تفويض علم حقيقته إليه تعالى. خلافا للمعتزلة.
ودليل وجوبِ الإيمانِ به: أنَّه من الأمور الممكنة التي ورد بها الكتاب، كقوله تعالى: ﴿فَاسْتَبَقُوا الصِّرَطَ﴾ [يس: ٦٦]، وفي السُّنَّة: «... فيضرب الصراط بين ظهراني جهنَّم، فأكون أنا وأمتي أوَّل مَن يجوز». واتفقت الكلمة عليه في الجملة، وكلُّ ما هو كذلك فالإيمان به واجبٌ. وطوله ثلاثة آلاف سنة: ألفُ صُعودٌ، وألف هبوطٌ، وألف استواء، وجبريل في أوَّله، وميكائيل.
قال القرافي والصحيح أنه عريض، وفيه طريقان، يمنى ويسرى، فأهل السَّعَادة يُسلَكُ بهم ذات اليمين، وأهل الشقاوة يُسلَك بهم ذات الشمال، وفيه طاقات، كل طاقة منها تنفذ إلى طبقة من طبقات جهنم. وقال بعضهم: أن الصراط يضيق ويتسع بحسب نور كل إنسان، فعرض كل صراطِ أحدٍ بقدر انتشار نوره، فإن نور كل إنسان لا يتعداه إلى غيره، فلا يمشي أحدٌ في نور أحد، ومن هنا كان دقيقا في حق قوم وعريضا في حق آخرين.
And the school of Ahl al-Sunna: keeping it (the Sirat) upon its apparent meaning, while delegating the knowledge of its reality to Him, exalted. Contrary to the Mu'tazila. And the evidence for the obligation of believing in it is that it is among possible matters that have been mentioned in the Book, such as His saying exalted: 'So they preceded to the Sirat' [Ya-Sin: 66], and in the Sunnah: '... then the Sirat is struck between the sides of Hell, so I and my community will be the first to cross.' And the consensus has agreed upon it in general. And everything that is like that, belief in it is obligatory. And its length is three thousand years: a thousand ascent, a thousand descent, and a thousand level, with Jibril at its beginning and Mika'il. Al-Qarafi said: the correct view is that it is broad, and in it are two paths: right and left. The people of happiness are made to take the right side, and the people of misery are made to take the left side. And in it are energies, each energy of which penetrates to a layer of the layers of Hell. And some said: that the Sirat narrows and widens according to the light of each person. So the width of each person's Sirat is according to the extent of the spread of his light. For the light of each person does not extend to another, so no one walks in the light of another. And from this it is narrow for some people and broad for others.
Source pages p. 541

Commentary
This passage sets out the Sunni position on the Sirat and provides the proof for obligatory belief. It begins by stating that Ahl al-Sunna affirm the literal meaning of the descriptions of the Sirat while delegating the exact reality to Allah (tafwid). This is contrary to the Mu'tazila who interpret it metaphorically. The evidence for the obligation of belief is that the Sirat is a possible matter (mumkin) mentioned in the Quran and Sunnah; the Quranic verse from Surah Ya-Sin and the hadith about the Prophet being the first to cross are cited. Since the community has agreed upon it in general, belief is obligatory. It then describes the Sirat's length as three thousand years: ascent, descent, and level, with angels at its beginning. A quote from al-Qarafi states the correct view is that it is broad, with two paths, and that it has branches leading to layers of Hell. Some scholars hold that the Sirat varies in width according to each person's light (nur) from their faith, so the narrowness or breadth is relative. This explanation shows how the Sirat can be both thin and broad depending on the believer's state.

Key Terms
مذهب أهل السنة
المعتزلة
تفويض
وجوب الإيمان
الصراط

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the Sirat is purely metaphorical and not a real, physical bridge.
Correction: The passage affirms the literal reality of the Sirat while leaving its true nature to Allah, opposing the metaphorical interpretation of the Mu'tazila.

Checkpoint
What is the evidence given in the passage for the obligation of believing in the Sirat?
A) It is mentioned in the Quran and Sunnah and agreed upon in general
B) It is a logical necessity

Key Takeaway
Belief in the Sirat is obligatory because it is affirmed by revelation and consensus, and Ahl al-Sunna affirm its literal descriptions while leaving the exact reality to Allah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The Sunni position is to affirm the literal descriptions while delegating the exact reality to Allah. In what areas of your life—especially concerning the unseen—do you find yourself leaning towards metaphorical interpretations to avoid the weight of belief? How can you train yourself to submit to the apparent meaning without demanding full comprehension?

Attributes of the Sirat: Length, Paths, and Light
Al-Azhari lists the traditional attributes of the Sirat.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the traditional description of the Sirat including its length, the presence of angels, the two paths, and how its width varies according to the believer's light.

Core Idea
The Sirat is a real, physical bridge with specific dimensions and features that reflect divine justice and individual faith.

After establishing the obligation of belief, Al-Azhari details the qualities of the Sirat as transmitted from the Salaf. He presents its length of three thousand years, the angels stationed at it, and the view of al-Qarafi regarding its breadth and the two paths. The lesson also explains the profound connection between a person's light (nur) and the apparent width of the Sirat.

Guided Path
1
Read the description of length
Notice the three-thousand-year span divided into ascent, descent, and level. This gives a sense of scale.
2
Note the presence of angels
Jibril and Mika'il are at the beginning of the Sirat. See how the author includes this detail without commentary.
3
Understand al-Qarafi's view
Al-Qarafi says the Sirat is broad, with two paths (right for the blessed, left for the wretched) and branches leading to layers of Hell.
This shows the Sirat's function in divine judgment.
4
Grasp the light-based variation
Some scholars state that the width of the Sirat depends on each person's light. The more light (faith), the wider it becomes for that person.
Reflect: how does this relate to the concept of individual accountability?
5
Synthesize the description
Notice that the passage combines multiple transmitted details without contradiction. The Sirat is both broad in itself and varying in experience.

The Sunni Doctrine on the Sirat and Its Proof
Author states Sunni doctrine of the Sirat and its proof of obligation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Sunni position on the Sirat (literal affirmation with tafwid) and the evidence that makes belief in it obligatory.

Core Idea
The Sirat is a real bridge over Hell; Ahl al-Sunna affirm it literally while entrusting its true nature to Allah.

The Sirat (bridge) is one of the sam'iyyat – matters known only through revelation. The author begins by stating the Sunni position, which differs from the Mu'tazila who interpret it metaphorically. He then provides the proof for its obligatory belief, drawing from the Quran, Sunnah, and consensus. This lesson establishes the doctrinal foundation before exploring its details.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Let the author's own words convey the position and proof.
2
Identify the Sunni position
Notice that Ahl al-Sunna affirm the Sirat literally on the surface, while consigning the true knowledge of its reality to Allah. This is known as tafwid.
Contrast with the Mu'tazila who reject the literal interpretation.
3
Understand the proof of obligation
The author gives three sources: Quranic verse, hadith, and consensus. Ask yourself why something being 'possible' and reported in revelation makes belief obligatory.
This connects to the broader principle that matters of the unseen must be accepted when confirmed by revelation.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قسم السمعيات ومذهب أهل السُّنَّة: إبقاؤه على ظاهره ، مع تفويض علم حقيقته إليه تعالى . خلافا للمعتزلة ودليل وجوبِ الإيمانِ به: أنَّه من الأمور الممكنة التي ورد بها الكتاب ، كقوله تعالى: ﴿فَاسْتَبَقُوا الصِّرَطَ﴾ [يس: ٦٦] ، وفي السُّنَّة: «... فيضرب الصراط بين ظهراني جهنَّم ، فأكون أنا وأمتي أوَّل مَن يجوز » واتفقت الكلمة عليه في الجملة ، وكلُّ ما هو كذلك فالإيمان به واجبٌ ، وطوله ثلاثة آلاف سنة: ألفُ صُعودٌ ، وألف هبوطٌ ، وألف استواء، وجبريل في أوَّله ، وميكائيل في وسطه، يَسألان النَّاسَ عن عُمرهم فيم أفنوه، وعن شَبَابِهم فيم أبلوه ، وعن علمهم ماذا عملوا به ، وفي حافتيه كَلَالِيبُ مُعلَّقة مأمورة بأخذ مَن أُمرتْ به وإذا وجب الإيمانُ به لثبوته فَالِعِبَادُ مُخْتَلِفٌ مُرُورُهمْ عليه ، أي : مُتفاوت في سُرعة النّجاة وعدمها، فليسوا فى المرور عليه على حَدِّ سواء، فشمل السَّبعين ألفا والنَّبيِّين والصدِّقين ، وخالف الحليمي في الكفار ؛ فذهب إلى أنَّهم لا يَمرُّون عليه فَسَالِمٌ أي : فمنهم فريقٌ سَالمٌ بعمله ، ناج مِن الوقوع في نار جهنَّم، وإِنْ خَدَشَتْهُ كَلالِيبُها وسقط وقامَ وجاوزَه بعد أعوام وَمُنْتَلِف، أي: ومنهم فريقٌ مُنتَلِف بعمله واقع في نار جهنم ؛ إما على الدوام والتأبيد كالكُفَّار والمنافقين، وإما إلى مُدَّة يُريدها الله تعالى ثُمَّ ينجو كبعض عُصاة المؤمنينَ ممَّن قضى الله عليه بالعذاب. والنَّجاةُ والهلاكُ بقدر الأعمال، فالنَّاجون هم أهل رُجحانِ الأعمال الصَّالحة ، والسَّالمون منهم من السيئات ممَّن خصهم الله بسابقة الحُسنَى، وهم الذين يجوزونَ كطَرْفِ العين، وبعدهم الذين يجُوزُونَ كالبَرْقِ الخَاطِفِ ، وبعدهُم الذين يجوزونَ كالرِّيح العَاصِف، وبعدهم الذين يجوزون كالطير، وبعدهم الذين يجُوزُونَ كالجواد السَّابق ، ثُمَّ الجَوازُ سعيا ومشيا، ومنهم مَن
Section of the Sam'iyyat (matters of the unseen). And the madhhab of Ahl al-Sunna: to leave it upon its apparent meaning, while consigning the knowledge of its reality to Him Most High. Contrary to the Mu'tazila. And the proof of the obligation of belief in it: that it is among possible matters reported by the Book, such as His saying, 'Then hasten to the bridge' [Ya Sin 66], and in the Sunna: '... then the bridge is placed across the middle of Hell, and I and my community will be the first to cross.' And the consensus word has agreed upon it in summary, and everything thus, belief in it is obligatory. And its length is three thousand years: a thousand ascent, a thousand descent, and a thousand level; Jibril is at its beginning, and Mika'il is in its midst, asking people about their lives: in what they spent them, about their youth: in what they consumed it, and about their knowledge: what they did with it. And on its sides are hooked barbs hanging, commanded to take whomever they are ordered. And when belief in it is obligatory because of its confirmation, so the servants — their crossing of it is diverse, i.e., varying in speed of deliverance and its lack, so they are not upon the same level in crossing it. Thus it includes the seventy thousand and the prophets and the veracious. And al-Halimi opposed concerning the disbelievers; he held that they do not cross it. So 'salim' (safe), i.e., there is a party safe by their deeds, delivered from falling into the fire of Hell, even if its hooks scratch them and they fall and rise and cross it after years. And 'muntalif' (perishing), i.e., there is a party perishing by their deeds, falling into the fire of Hell, either perpetually and eternally like the disbelievers and hypocrites, or for a period God wills then they are saved, like some disobedient believers whom God decreed punishment. And deliverance and destruction are according to deeds. So the delivered are the people of preponderance of righteous deeds, and the safe among them from sins are those whom God singled out with prior favor, and they are the ones who cross like the blink of an eye, and after them those who cross like the flashing lightning, and after them those who cross like the violent wind, and after them those who cross like the bird, and after them those who cross like the racing horse, then crossing by running and walking, and among them is he who
Source pages p. 541

Commentary
This passage is a definition and proof of the Sunni doctrine regarding the Sirat (the bridge over Hell). The author begins by stating the madhhab of Ahl al-Sunna: they affirm the bridge as a literal reality, consigning its true nature to God, contrary to the Mu'tazila who interpret it metaphorically. Then he gives the proof for its obligatory belief: it is a possible matter reported in the Quran and Sunna, and consensus has affirmed it, so belief is wajib. He then describes its length—three thousand years—and that Jibril and Mika'il are positioned at its beginning and middle, questioning people. The bridge has hooked barbs. After confirming obligation, he explains that people differ in crossing: some are safe (salim) and some perish (muntalif). Safety and destruction depend on deeds. The fastest cross like a blink, then lightning, wind, bird, racing horse, then running and walking. The passage ends mid-sentence, likely with further detail.

السَّمعِيَّات
التَّفْوِيض
المُعْتَزِلَة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Mu'tazila claim the Sirat is a metaphor and not a literal bridge.
Correction: Ahl al-Sunna affirm it as a real bridge over Hell, while consigning its true nature to Allah.

Key Takeaway
Belief in the Sirat is obligatory because it is a possible matter affirmed by revelation and consensus, and Ahl al-Sunna affirm it literally while leaving its true nature to Allah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Is there any unseen matter (like the Sirat, the scales, or the punishment of the grave) that you find yourself hesitating to fully believe in because your mind cannot grasp it? How does this lesson confront your reluctance, and what specific action will you take this week to strengthen your conviction in that matter?
?
The author proves that belief in the Sirat is obligatory solely because it is reported in revelation and consensus—not because we understand its reality. Does your faith rely more on what makes sense to you personally or on the authority of Allah and His Messenger? Be honest: where do you secretly prefer your own reason over revelation?
?
The Mu'tazila denied the literal Sirat because it seemed impossible to them. What 'impossible' thing in your life (a trial, a command, or an unseen reality) are you tempted to reinterpret rather than submit? Will you entrust its true knowledge to Allah and obey despite your confusion?

Description of the Sirat and the Diversity of Crossing
Author describes the Sirat's attributes and the varying states of crossing.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the detailed description of the Sirat (its length, angels, hooks) and how people's crossing varies in speed and outcome (salim vs muntalif).

Core Idea
The Sirat is three thousand years long, guarded by angels, and people cross it according to their deeds—some swiftly, some slowly, and some perish.

After establishing the obligation of belief, the author provides a vivid description of the Sirat: its immense length, the angels Jibril and Mika'il at its ends, and the hooked barbs on its sides. He then explains that people's crossing is not uniform; some are safe (salim) and some perish (muntalif), and within the safe, there are varying speeds. This lesson details the eschatological reality of the Sirat.

Guided Path
1
Read the description of the Sirat
Read the passage carefully, noting the three components: length, the angels Jibril and Mika'il, and the hooked barbs.
The length is given in years as ascent, descent, and level.
2
Identify the diversity of crossing
The author states that people are not equal in crossing. Look for the two main categories: salim (safe) and muntalif (perishing). Note al-Halimi's view on disbelievers.
3
Note the speeds of the safe
The passage lists several speeds: blink of eye, lightning, wind, bird, horse, running, walking. Reflect on how this shows gradation based on deeds.
This emphasizes that salvation is by God's grace and one's deeds.

قسم السمعيات ومذهب أهل السُّنَّة: إبقاؤه على ظاهره ، مع تفويض علم حقيقته إليه تعالى . خلافا للمعتزلة ودليل وجوبِ الإيمانِ به: أنَّه من الأمور الممكنة التي ورد بها الكتاب ، كقوله تعالى: ﴿فَاسْتَبَقُوا الصِّرَطَ﴾ [يس: ٦٦] ، وفي السُّنَّة: «... فيضرب الصراط بين ظهراني جهنَّم ، فأكون أنا وأمتي أوَّل مَن يجوز » واتفقت الكلمة عليه في الجملة ، وكلُّ ما هو كذلك فالإيمان به واجبٌ ، وطوله ثلاثة آلاف سنة: ألفُ صُعودٌ ، وألف هبوطٌ ، وألف استواء، وجبريل في أوَّله ، وميكائيل في وسطه، يَسألان النَّاسَ عن عُمرهم فيم أفنوه، وعن شَبَابِهم فيم أبلوه ، وعن علمهم ماذا عملوا به ، وفي حافتيه كَلَالِيبُ مُعلَّقة مأمورة بأخذ مَن أُمرتْ به وإذا وجب الإيمانُ به لثبوته فَالِعِبَادُ مُخْتَلِفٌ مُرُورُهمْ عليه ، أي : مُتفاوت في سُرعة النّجاة وعدمها، فليسوا فى المرور عليه على حَدِّ سواء، فشمل السَّبعين ألفا والنَّبيِّين والصدِّقين ، وخالف الحليمي في الكفار ؛ فذهب إلى أنَّهم لا يَمرُّون عليه فَسَالِمٌ أي : فمنهم فريقٌ سَالمٌ بعمله ، ناج مِن الوقوع في نار جهنَّم، وإِنْ خَدَشَتْهُ كَلالِيبُها وسقط وقامَ وجاوزَه بعد أعوام وَمُنْتَلِف، أي: ومنهم فريقٌ مُنتَلِف بعمله واقع في نار جهنم ؛ إما على الدوام والتأبيد كالكُفَّار والمنافقين، وإما إلى مُدَّة يُريدها الله تعالى ثُمَّ ينجو كبعض عُصاة المؤمنينَ ممَّن قضى الله عليه بالعذاب. والنَّجاةُ والهلاكُ بقدر الأعمال، فالنَّاجون هم أهل رُجحانِ الأعمال الصَّالحة ، والسَّالمون منهم من السيئات ممَّن خصهم الله بسابقة الحُسنَى، وهم الذين يجوزونَ كطَرْفِ العين، وبعدهم الذين يجُوزُونَ كالبَرْقِ الخَاطِفِ ، وبعدهُم الذين يجوزونَ كالرِّيح العَاصِف، وبعدهم الذين يجوزون كالطير، وبعدهم الذين يجُوزُونَ كالجواد السَّابق ، ثُمَّ الجَوازُ سعيا ومشيا، ومنهم مَن
Section of the Sam'iyyat (matters of the unseen). And the madhhab of Ahl al-Sunna: to leave it upon its apparent meaning, while consigning the knowledge of its reality to Him Most High. Contrary to the Mu'tazila. And the proof of the obligation of belief in it: that it is among possible matters reported by the Book, such as His saying, 'Then hasten to the bridge' [Ya Sin 66], and in the Sunna: '... then the bridge is placed across the middle of Hell, and I and my community will be the first to cross.' And the consensus word has agreed upon it in summary, and everything thus, belief in it is obligatory. And its length is three thousand years: a thousand ascent, a thousand descent, and a thousand level; Jibril is at its beginning, and Mika'il is in its midst, asking people about their lives: in what they spent them, about their youth: in what they consumed it, and about their knowledge: what they did with it. And on its sides are hooked barbs hanging, commanded to take whomever they are ordered. And when belief in it is obligatory because of its confirmation, so the servants — their crossing of it is diverse, i.e., varying in speed of deliverance and its lack, so they are not upon the same level in crossing it. Thus it includes the seventy thousand and the prophets and the veracious. And al-Halimi opposed concerning the disbelievers; he held that they do not cross it. So 'salim' (safe), i.e., there is a party safe by their deeds, delivered from falling into the fire of Hell, even if its hooks scratch them and they fall and rise and cross it after years. And 'muntalif' (perishing), i.e., there is a party perishing by their deeds, falling into the fire of Hell, either perpetually and eternally like the disbelievers and hypocrites, or for a period God wills then they are saved, like some disobedient believers whom God decreed punishment. And deliverance and destruction are according to deeds. So the delivered are the people of preponderance of righteous deeds, and the safe among them from sins are those whom God singled out with prior favor, and they are the ones who cross like the blink of an eye, and after them those who cross like the flashing lightning, and after them those who cross like the violent wind, and after them those who cross like the bird, and after them those who cross like the racing horse, then crossing by running and walking, and among them is he who
Source pages p. 541

Commentary
This passage is a definition and proof of the Sunni doctrine regarding the Sirat (the bridge over Hell). The author begins by stating the madhhab of Ahl al-Sunna: they affirm the bridge as a literal reality, consigning its true nature to God, contrary to the Mu'tazila who interpret it metaphorically. Then he gives the proof for its obligatory belief: it is a possible matter reported in the Quran and Sunna, and consensus has affirmed it, so belief is wajib. He then describes its length—three thousand years—and that Jibril and Mika'il are positioned at its beginning and middle, questioning people. The bridge has hooked barbs. After confirming obligation, he explains that people differ in crossing: some are safe (salim) and some perish (muntalif). Safety and destruction depend on deeds. The fastest cross like a blink, then lightning, wind, bird, racing horse, then running and walking. The passage ends mid-sentence, likely with further detail.

السَّالِم
المنْتَلِف
الكَفَّار
المنافقين

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think all people cross the Sirat in the same manner or speed.
Correction: The author emphasizes that crossing varies greatly: some are safe, some perish, and speeds differ according to deeds.

A) They cross quickly.

C) They cross slowly.
D) They are not affected by hooks.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The passage says people cross the Sirat according to their deeds. What specific deed in your life right now—if left unchecked—would most likely cause you to fall or slow you down? Will you commit to leaving it today?
?
Even some believers will fall into the fire temporarily. Does that reality unsettle you? How are you actively preparing to be among those who cross 'like the blink of an eye'?
?
Jibril and Mika'il will question you about your youth, your life, and your knowledge. If you were asked right now, would your answer please Allah? What will you change starting today so that your answer brings you safety, not loss?

The Sirat and the Obligatory Belief in Its Crossing
Describes the Sirat and the obligatory belief in diverse crossing.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the physical description of the Sirat (questioning angels and hooks), the obligation to believe in the diversity of crossing, and the controversy over whether disbelievers cross.

Core Idea
The Sirat has hooks and questioning angels; belief in varied crossing is obligatory.

This passage introduces the Sirat as a bridge with questioning angels and hooks. It establishes that belief in the Sirat is mandatory and that believers and unbelievers differ in their crossing. It also addresses al-Halimi’s claim that disbelievers do not cross at all and resolves it by explaining they cross part of it then fall.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic once to get the overall flow: description of the Sirat, then obligation, then the variance, then al-Halimi’s objection.
Notice the detail about the questioning angels in the middle and hooks on the sides.
2
Identify the obligation and the variance
Focus on the phrase 'وإذا وجب الإيمان به' and the statement that people’s crossing is varied. Understand that this is a matter of belief.
The variance includes speed of deliverance.
3
Understand the scope of those crossing
The passage says the variance includes the seventy thousand, prophets, and truthful. Al-Halimi held that disbelievers do not cross at all.
4
Resolve the controversy
Read the footnote explaining that disbelievers cross part of the Sirat then fall. This is the agreed-upon view.
Al-Halimi's view is interpreted as referring to a specific group thrown directly into Hell.

The passing of the servants over the Sirat: in its middle, they (the angels) ask people about their lifespan in what they spent it, and about their youth in what they wore it out, and about their knowledge what they did with it. On its sides are hooks suspended, commanded to take whom they are commanded. And when belief in it is obligatory due to its confirmation, (then the servants) meaning: it is obligatory to believe that all those charged with duties, whether believers or not, (their passing over it is varied) i.e., varying in speed of deliverance and lack thereof, so they are not all equal in passing over it. So it includes the seventy thousand, the prophets, and the truthful. Al-Halimi disagreed regarding the disbelievers; he held that they do not pass over it. (1) His statement: (He held that they do not pass over it. The author added in al-Kabir: Yes, it can be interpreted as during the passing not its beginning. So the meaning is that they do not pass over all of it, rather over part of it then they fall. And you are aware that this is agreed upon, so there is no sense in singling out al-Halimi. Perhaps he meant the group that is thrown into Hell in a heap from the forelocks and feet from the standing place without a Sirat.) — al-Amir and al-Shanwani. Section of Sam'iyyat. He who passes over it crawling, and their variation in passing is according to their variation in turning away from the sacred things of God when they occur to their hearts. So whoever among them was quicker in turning away from what God has forbidden was quicker in passing on that Day. .. And the light of each person on the Sirat does not extend to others; no one walks in the light of another. And the Sirat widens and narrows (1) according to the spread and constriction of the light. So the width of each person's Sirat is according to the spread of his light. Hence it is narrow for some people and wide for others, while it is one in itself. On this basis is derived what is reported that it is a journey of three thousand years. The wisdom in it: the appearance of deliverance from the Fire, and that Paradise becomes more joyful to their hearts afterwards, and so that the disbeliever regrets the success of the believers after their sharing in the graves. (1) His statement: (And the Sirat widens and narrows — this contradicts what preceded that it is finer... and al-Badr al-Zarkashi said that. In some narrations it is finer than a hair and sharper than a sword. If it is confirmed, it is not taken at face value because it conflicts with other hadiths about angels standing on its sides, the hooks and thorns in it, and giving each passer from the light the measure of the place of his feet.) — al-Shanwani.
Source pages p. 542

Commentary
This passage is a detailed exposition on the nature of the Sirat (bridge over Hell) and the varying circumstances of people crossing it. The author begins by describing the Sirat: in its middle, two angels question people about their lives (how they spent their time, youth, and knowledge). On the sides are hooks that seize anyone commanded to be thrown into Hell. Then the author explains that belief in the Sirat is obligatory, and that people differ in their crossing: some are safe, others are seized. The speed of deliverance varies. The author mentions that al-Halimi held that disbelievers do not cross at all, but a footnote clarifies that they only cross partly before falling, which is agreed upon. Then the passage discusses the varying speeds: some pass like the blinking of an eye, like lightning, like wind, like birds, like a galloping horse, then walking, crawling, all according to their turning away from forbidden things. Further, the author states that each person has a personal light that does not extend to others. The Sirat itself is one, but it appears narrow or wide according to each person's light. The wisdom behind this is to manifest deliverance and increase joy in Paradise, and to cause regret for disbelievers.

الصراط
الكلاليب
المُرور
الحليمي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Disbelievers do not cross the Sirat at all.
Correction: The correct view is that they cross part of it then fall, as agreed upon.

Checkpoint

C) Their faith and deeds

Key Takeaway
The Sirat has questioning angels and hooks; belief in varied crossing is obligatory, and even disbelievers cross partially before falling.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The angels on the Sirat will ask you about your lifespan: in what did you spend it? Think of the last week — how many hours did you spend in acts that will please Allah on that day? Isn't it terrifying that each moment will be accounted for? What will your answer be? Write down one change you will make today to use your time better.
?
Your youth—how have you worn it out? Have you used it for good or wasted it? If the Sirat were before you now, would you be among those who cross swiftly or those who are caught by the hooks? What must change today? Make a firm intention to use your remaining youth in obedience.
?
You have learned this lesson about the Sirat. The angels will ask about your knowledge: what did you do with it? Will you merely memorize it, or will it change your heart and actions? Make a concrete intention now: how will this belief in the Sirat affect your behavior today? Write it down and commit.

The Light of Each Person and the Width of the Sirat
Explains the variation in crossing speed and the effect of each person's light on the Sirat's width.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the speed of crossing correlates with one's avoidance of sin, and how each person's light affects the width of the Sirat.

Core Idea
The faster you turn away from sin, the faster you cross; your light determines the width of the Sirat.

In this passage, the author explains that people cross the Sirat at varying speeds, from crawling to quicker paces, depending on how quickly they turn away from forbidden things. Then he elaborates on the light of each believer—a personal light that does not extend to others—and how it makes the Sirat appear wide or narrow for each person. The passage concludes with the wisdom behind this arrangement.

Guided Path
1
Read about the crawling example
The passage starts with 'يجوزه حبوا' (he who passes over it crawling). This sets the stage for the principle of variation.
2
Understand the principle of variation
The speed of crossing is directly linked to how quickly a person turns away from God's prohibitions when they occur to the heart.
This is an internal moral/spiritual quality, not physical speed.
3
Study the light on the Sirat
Each person has a light that only illuminates for them; no one can walk in another's light. The Sirat's width for each is determined by the spread of that light.
The Sirat itself is one, but appears wide or narrow accordingly.
4
Ponder the wisdom
The wisdom includes manifesting deliverance from the Fire, making Paradise more joyful, and causing disbelievers to regret.

The passing of the servants over the Sirat: in its middle, they (the angels) ask people about their lifespan in what they spent it, and about their youth in what they wore it out, and about their knowledge what they did with it. On its sides are hooks suspended, commanded to take whom they are commanded. And when belief in it is obligatory due to its confirmation, (then the servants) meaning: it is obligatory to believe that all those charged with duties, whether believers or not, (their passing over it is varied) i.e., varying in speed of deliverance and lack thereof, so they are not all equal in passing over it. So it includes the seventy thousand, the prophets, and the truthful. Al-Halimi disagreed regarding the disbelievers; he held that they do not pass over it. (1) His statement: (He held that they do not pass over it. The author added in al-Kabir: Yes, it can be interpreted as during the passing not its beginning. So the meaning is that they do not pass over all of it, rather over part of it then they fall. And you are aware that this is agreed upon, so there is no sense in singling out al-Halimi. Perhaps he meant the group that is thrown into Hell in a heap from the forelocks and feet from the standing place without a Sirat.) — al-Amir and al-Shanwani. Section of Sam'iyyat. He who passes over it crawling, and their variation in passing is according to their variation in turning away from the sacred things of God when they occur to their hearts. So whoever among them was quicker in turning away from what God has forbidden was quicker in passing on that Day. .. And the light of each person on the Sirat does not extend to others; no one walks in the light of another. And the Sirat widens and narrows (1) according to the spread and constriction of the light. So the width of each person's Sirat is according to the spread of his light. Hence it is narrow for some people and wide for others, while it is one in itself. On this basis is derived what is reported that it is a journey of three thousand years. The wisdom in it: the appearance of deliverance from the Fire, and that Paradise becomes more joyful to their hearts afterwards, and so that the disbeliever regrets the success of the believers after their sharing in the graves. (1) His statement: (And the Sirat widens and narrows — this contradicts what preceded that it is finer... and al-Badr al-Zarkashi said that. In some narrations it is finer than a hair and sharper than a sword. If it is confirmed, it is not taken at face value because it conflicts with other hadiths about angels standing on its sides, the hooks and thorns in it, and giving each passer from the light the measure of the place of his feet.) — al-Shanwani.
Source pages p. 542

Commentary
This passage is a detailed exposition on the nature of the Sirat (bridge over Hell) and the varying circumstances of people crossing it. The author begins by describing the Sirat: in its middle, two angels question people about their lives (how they spent their time, youth, and knowledge). On the sides are hooks that seize anyone commanded to be thrown into Hell. Then the author explains that belief in the Sirat is obligatory, and that people differ in their crossing: some are safe, others are seized. The speed of deliverance varies. The author mentions that al-Halimi held that disbelievers do not cross at all, but a footnote clarifies that they only cross partly before falling, which is agreed upon. Then the passage discusses the varying speeds: some pass like the blinking of an eye, like lightning, like wind, like birds, like a galloping horse, then walking, crawling, all according to their turning away from forbidden things. Further, the author states that each person has a personal light that does not extend to others. The Sirat itself is one, but it appears narrow or wide according to each person's light. The wisdom behind this is to manifest deliverance and increase joy in Paradise, and to cause regret for disbelievers.

Key Terms
النور
الصراط
النجاة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All people cross the Sirat in the same manner.
Correction: This passage emphasizes that people cross at varying speeds and the Sirat appears different widths for each according to their light.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what determines the width of the Sirat for each person?
A) The number of good deeds
B) The spread of their light
C) The speed of their crossing
D) Their physical strength

Key Takeaway
Each person's speed on the Sirat depends on how quickly they turn away from sin, and the width of the Sirat for each is determined by their personal light.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When a forbidden thought enters your mind, how quickly do you turn away? Does your hesitation reveal a weakness that will slow you down on the Sirat? What habit can you change right now to train your heart to turn away faster?
?
Your light on the Sirat is entirely yours. Are you actively increasing its spread through taqwa, or are you letting worldly distractions dim it? What will you do today to make your light wider for that day?
?
The Sirat is narrow for some and wide for others, though it is one. On that day, which group will you belong to? Look at your life honestly: what is one sin you keep returning to that is shrinking your light? Will you truly turn away from it now?

Belief in the Throne, Kursi, Pen, Tablet, and Recording Angels
States the obligation to believe in five created entities and describes the Throne.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the obligation to believe in five specific created entities mentioned in revelation: the Throne, the Kursi, the Pen, the Tablet, and the recording angels, and you will know the description of the Throne as a great luminous body.

Core Idea
Belief in the unseen entities like the Throne is an obligation for every Muslim.

This lesson introduces a set of articles of faith that are known from the Qur'an and Sunnah, namely the Throne, Kursi, Pen, Tablet, and recording angels. While these are not objects of rational deduction, they are real created things that we must affirm. The passage also provides a brief description of the Throne, clarifying its nature as a physical, luminous body.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then read the literal translation. Notice how the passage begins by stating the obligation and then describes the Throne.
The passage includes a verse line from the poem.
2
Identify the five entities
List the five created entities mentioned: the Throne, the Kursi, the Pen, the Tablet, and the recording angels. Each is an object of belief.
Only the Throne is described; the others are named but not elaborated here.
3
Study the description of the Throne
Focus on how the Throne is defined: a great luminous body, lofty, encompassing all bodies. Note the two views on its shape: spherical according to astronomers, or a dome according to the well-known Sunni view.
The Throne is carried now by four angels and on Judgment Day by eight.

(۲) قوله: (نوراني) أي: ذو نور، (۳) قوله: (محيط) هذا على قول أهل الهيئة بكرويته ، ومشهور السنة أنه قبة عظيمة ، يحمله الآن أربعة ويوم القيامة ثمانية ؛ لعظم التجلي الأمير .
Clarification of the obligation of belief in the Throne, the Kursi, the Tablet, the Pen, and the writers. The Pen and the writers, the Tablet, all wisdom. 107 - And the Throne and the Kursi, then the Pen. (And the Throne) and it is: a great luminous body, lofty, encompassing all bodies. (2) His statement: (luminous) i.e., possessing light, (3) His statement: (encompassing) this is according to the view of the astronomers of its sphericity, and the well-known view of the Sunnah is that it is a great dome, carried now by four (angels) and on the Day of Resurrection by eight, due to the greatness of the manifestation. — al-Amir.
Source pages p. 543

Commentary
This passage is a declarative statement of the obligation to believe in five specific created entities: the Throne (al-'Arsh), the Kursi, the Pen (al-Qalam), the Tablet (al-Lawh), and the recording angels (al-Katibun). The author presents this as a heading, then quotes a verse from the poem (line 107) that mentions the Throne, Kursi, and Pen. The commentary then defines the Throne: it is a great luminous body, high, and encompassing all bodies. Two footnotes clarify the nature of its 'luminous' (it has light, not that its essence is light) and its 'encompassing' shape: the astronomers say it is spherical, but the well-known Sunni position is that it is a great dome, currently carried by four angels and on the Day of Judgment by eight. This teaches that belief in these entities is part of the sam'iyyat (matters heard from revelation) and must be accepted as true.

Correction: The Throne is a real, luminous, physical body as affirmed by the Sunnah, not a metaphor.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You recite 'He who created death and life' (Quran 67:2) — but do you truly believe that every moment of your life is being recorded by angels who are writing right now? How would you live differently if you were constantly aware of this recording? What will you change starting today?
?
The Throne is a real, luminous body so vast it encompasses all creation. When you pray, do you feel the majesty of the One above the Throne? Or have your prayers become routine, forgetting that you stand before the Lord of the Throne? What practical step can you take to bring that awe into your next prayer?
?
Part of your iman (faith) is believing in the Pen that wrote your destiny. When trials come, do you accept them as already written, or do you complain against what was destined? Identify one recent trial and ask yourself: 'Did I submit to Allah's decree, or did I resist it?' What will you do to strengthen your trust in the Pen's writing?

The Sirat: Width Varies by Light
Commentator explains Sirat's width variation based on light

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the Sirat (bridge over Hell) is one physical bridge, but its apparent width varies for each believer according to the spread of their light, which corresponds to their piety in turning away from forbidden things.

Core Idea
The Sirat's width depends on each person's light, not on the bridge itself.

The commentator explains why the crossing of the Sirat varies among believers. He ties the speed of crossing to how quickly they turned away from forbidden things during life, and the width of the bridge to the spread of each person's light. This lesson unpacks these connections and the wisdom behind the variation, as well as a clarification about hadith that describe the Sirat as finer than a hair.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Start by reading the Arabic passage and its literal translation. Pay attention to the flow of ideas: crossing, variation according to turning away, light individuality, width variation, and the footnote.
The footnote is part of the scholarly commentary and addresses an apparent contradiction.
2
Identify the key factors
Notice the two factors that determine crossing speed and bridge width: how quickly one turned away from forbidden things, and the spread of one's light. The light is individual and does not help others.
The light is a metaphor for spiritual illumination gained by piety.
3
Understand the wisdom
Reflect on the three wisdoms mentioned: to show deliverance from Fire, to increase joy in Paradise, and to cause regret for disbelievers.
These explain why the variation exists despite the bridge being one.
4
Examine the footnote
Read the footnote about the hadith describing the Sirat as finer than a hair. Understand that this is not taken literally due to conflicting hadith about angels and hooks.
This shows how kalam scholars reconcile apparent contradictions in transmitted texts.

Source Text

(۱) قوله : ( ويتسع الصراط ويدق هذا خلاف ما تقدم من أنه أدقُ ... وبذلك قال البدر الزركشي، وفي بعض الروايات أنه أدقّ من الشعرة وأحد من السيف» فإن ثبت فهي غير محمولة على ظاهرها لمنافاتها للأحاديث الأخرى من قيام الملائكة على جنبيه، وكون الكلاليب والحسك فيه ، وإعطاء كل من المارين عليه من النور قدر موضع قدميه . الشنواني .
They cross it crawling, and their variation in passing is according to their variation in turning away from the sanctities of God when they occur to their hearts. Whoever among them is quicker to turn away from what God has forbidden is quicker in crossing on that day. And the light of each person on the bridge does not extend to another, so no one walks in the light of another. The bridge widens and narrows (1) according to the spread and constriction of light. So the width of each person's bridge is proportionate to the spread of his light. Hence it is narrow for some people and wide for others, while it is one in itself. On this is based what is reported that it is a journey of three thousand years. The wisdom in it is the manifestation of deliverance from the Fire, and that Paradise becomes more joyous to their hearts afterwards, and that the disbeliever may regret the believers' success after they shared in the graves. (1) His saying: 'It widens and narrows' contradicts what preceded that it is finer... and al-Badr al-Zarkashi said that. In some narrations it is finer than a hair and sharper than a sword. If that is established, it is not taken literally because it conflicts with other hadiths about angels standing on its sides, and the hooks and thorns in it, and giving each of those who cross it light the size of his footsteps. al-Shanwani.
Source pages p. 543

Commentary
This passage explains the variation in crossing the Sirat (bridge) on the Day of Judgment. It states that people cross it crawling, and their speed depends on how quickly they turned away from forbidden things in life. Each person has their own light that does not benefit others. The bridge's width varies according to the light: wider for those with more light, narrower for those with less. Despite this, the bridge is one entity. The reported length of three thousand years is explained as consistent with this variation. The wisdom includes showing who is saved, increasing joy for believers, and causing regret for disbelievers. The footnote clarifies that reports of the bridge being finer than a hair are not literal, as they conflict with other hadiths describing angels and hooks on it.

Misconception & Correction

Correction: The Sirat is one physical bridge, but its perceived width varies according to each person's light. The variation is in the experience, not the bridge itself.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

Think of the last time a temptation or a sinful thought crossed your mind. How quickly did you dismiss it? What does that reveal about your light on the bridge?
?
Your light is yours alone — no one else's light can help you on the Sirat. If you were to see the size of your light right now based on your present state of turning away from prohibitions, would it be enough to widen the bridge for you? What specific sin are you currently tolerating that is dimming that light?
?
The bridge is one, but it becomes wide or narrow according to your light. You cannot change its nature, but you can change your light. What concrete step will you take today to increase the speed of your turning away from God's prohibitions, so that your crossing on that day is swift and wide?

Belief in the Throne, Footstool, Pen, Tablet, and Recording Angels
Commentator defines the five eschatological objects and their nature.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the five eschatological objects mentioned in the poem (Throne, Footstool, Pen, Tablet, Recording Angels) and the commentator's approach of refraining from defining their exact nature due to lack of knowledge.

Core Idea
We must believe in these objects but cannot fully know their reality.

The commentator begins by listing the five objects that every Muslim must believe in: the Throne, Footstool, Pen, Tablet, and Recording Angels. He then defines each as a luminous body, but importantly, he refrains from specifying their exact nature because such knowledge is beyond human reach. This lesson will walk you through these definitions and the wise principle of 'tawaqquf' (suspending judgment) on matters not revealed in detail.

Guided Path
1
Identify the five objects
Read the passage and list the five eschatological objects that are obligatory to believe in. Notice the order in which they are mentioned.
The order is: Throne, Footstool, Pen, Recording Angels, Tablet.
2
Understand the definitions
For each object, note the common description: 'a great luminous body.' Observe the details given for each, such as the Throne encompassing all bodies and the Footstool being attached to the Throne above the seventh heaven.
The Recording Angels are divided into three categories.
3
Recognize the principle of tawaqquf
Notice the repeated phrase 'we refrain from deciding its reality' (نمسك عن القطع بتعيين حقيقته). Reflect on why the commentator refrains from defining the exact nature of these objects.
This shows humility before divine knowledge.
4
Contrast with a common misunderstanding
The passage explicitly states that the Footstool is not the Throne, contrary to the opinion of al-Hasan al-Basri. Appreciate that these are distinct creations of Allah.

Statement of the obligation of belief in the Throne, the Footstool, the Tablet, the Pen, and the scribes. The Pen and the scribes, the Tablet, all are wisdom. 107 - The Throne and the Footstool, then the Pen. (The Throne) is a great luminous body, high, encompassing all bodies. (1) His saying: 'It widens and narrows...' (as before). (2) His saying: 'luminous' meaning possessing light. (3) His saying: 'encompassing' is according to astronomers that it is spherical, but the well-known view of the Ahl al-Sunna is that it is a great dome, carried now by four and on the Day of Judgment by eight, due to the greatness of the manifestation. al-Amir. Obligation of belief in the Throne, the Footstool, the Tablet, the Pen. It is said: It is the first of created things in concrete existence; we refrain from deciding its reality for lack of knowledge. (The Footstool) is a great luminous body before the Throne, attached to it above the seventh heaven; we refrain from deciding its reality for lack of knowledge, and it is not the Throne, contrary to al-Hasan. (1) His saying: 'concrete' meaning external. al-Shanwani. (2) al-Hasan ibn Abi al-Hasan al-Basri... (biography). (3) In some copies: 'and He commanded it to write.' (4) His saying: 'and the scribes from the Tablet' means they copy from the Preserved Tablet the decrees of matters to the scrolls of the angels entrusted with management every year; so the scribes are three categories. al-Shanwani. Then the Pen is a great luminous body, God created it and commanded it to write what was and what will be until the Day of Resurrection; we refrain from affirming its reality. (And) the angels (the scribes) over the servants record their deeds in this world, and the scribes from the Preserved Tablet copy what is in the scrolls of the angels entrusted with management in the world, and the scribes from the scrolls of the guardians write a book placed under the Throne. (And the Tablet) is a luminous body on which the Pen wrote by God's permission what was and what will be until the Hour; we refrain from affirming its reality.

Commentary
This passage begins by asserting the obligation to believe in six things: the Throne ('Arsh), the Footstool (Kursi), the Pen (Qalam), the Recording Angels (Kaatibun), and the Tablet (Lawh). It quotes the poem line and then defines each. The Throne is a great luminous body encompassing all others; a footnote notes the conflicting views on its shape (spherical vs. dome) and that it will be carried by eight angels on Judgment Day. The Footstool is a luminous body attached to the Throne above the seventh heaven; it is distinct from the Throne, contrary to al-Hasan al-Basri. The Pen is a great luminous body commanded to write all destinies. The Recording Angels are three categories: those who record deeds, those who copy from the Preserved Tablet to the scrolls of managing angels, and those who compile a book under the Throne. The Tablet is a luminous body on which the Pen wrote everything by God's permission. For each, the author refrains from dogmatically defining its exact reality due to lack of knowledge, except for the Throne and Footstool where he states they are bodies.

Belief in the Divine Entities: The Throne, Kursi, Pen, Tablet, and Recording Angels
Describes the obligation of belief in the 'Arsh, Kursi, Pen, Tablet, and writing angels.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the obligation to believe in the 'Arsh, Kursi, Pen, Tablet, and writing angels, and why we must refrain from claiming definitive knowledge of their true reality.

Core Idea
We believe in these unseen entities but admit our ignorance of their exact reality.

This passage from the Jawharat al-Tawhid commentary establishes the obligation to have faith in several key entities mentioned in the Quran and Sunnah: the Throne, the Footstool, the Pen, the Tablet, and the recording angels. The author follows a consistent method: he briefly describes each entity using the revealed descriptions, then immediately cautions that we cannot definitively know their true nature. This teaches us a balanced approach of affirmation without overstepping our knowledge.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the entities
Read the Arabic and translation. Notice the pattern: each entity is introduced, briefly described, and then followed by a statement of withholding judgment.
2
Examine the descriptions of each entity
Look at how each entity is described (great luminous body, etc.). What do they have in common? The descriptions are minimal and from revelation. Also note the refutation of al-Hasan al-Basri regarding the Kursi.
3
Understand the theological principle of 'imskak'
The repeated phrase 'نُمسك عن الجزم بتعيين حقيقته' teaches us an important principle: we affirm existence but refrain from speculating about reality. Reflect on why this is crucial in kalam to avoid anthropomorphism or denial.
This principle is a recurring theme in Sunni creed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وجوب الإيمان بالعرش والكرسي واللوح والقلم قيل : هو أوَّل المخلوقات وجودًا عَيْنِيًّا ، نُمسِكُ عن القطع بتعيين حقيقته ؛ لعدم العلم بها . والكُرْسِيُّ وهو : جِسمٌ عظيمٌ نُورَاني بين يدي العرش ، مُلتصق به فوق السَّماء السَّابعة ، نُمْسِك عن القطع بتعيين حقيقته ؛ لعدم العلم بها، وهو غير العرش ، خلافًا للحسن . ثُمَّ القَلَمُ وهو جسمٌ عظيم نوراني ، خَلَقَهُ اللهُ تعالى وأَمَرَهُ بكَتُب ما كانَ وما يكونُ إلى يوم القيامة ، نُمْسِكُ عن الجزم بتعيين حقيقته . والملائكةُ الكَاتِبُونَ على العِباد أعمالَهُم في الدُّنيا، والكاتبون من اللوح المحفوظ ما في صُحف الملائكة الموكلين بالتصرف في العالم، والكاتبون مِن صُحف الحفظة كتابا يوضع تحت العرش. واللَّوْحُ وهو: جسمٌ نُورَانِي كَتبَ فيه القلَمُ بإِذنِ الله ما كان وما هو كائن إلى قيام الساعة ، نُمسك عن الجزم بتعيين حقيقته .
The obligation of faith in the Throne, the Kursi, the Tablet, and the Pen. It is said: It is the first of created things in concrete existence. We refrain from definitively determining its reality due to lack of knowledge of it. And the Kursi: it is a great luminous body between the hands of the Throne, attached to it above the seventh heaven. We refrain from definitively determining its reality due to lack of knowledge of it, and it is other than the Throne, contrary to al-Hasan. Then the Pen: it is a great luminous body which God Almighty created and commanded to write what was and what will be until the Day of Resurrection. We refrain from definitively determining its reality. And the angels, the writers of the deeds of the servants in this world, and the writers from the Preserved Tablet of what is in the scrolls of the angels entrusted with disposal in the world, and the writers from the scrolls of the guardian angels of a book placed under the Throne. And the Tablet: it is a luminous body on which the Pen wrote by God's permission what was and what will be until the Hour is established. We refrain from definitively determining its reality.
Source pages p. 544

Commentary
This passage defines the obligation of belief in the Throne (al-‘Arsh), the Footstool (al-Kursi), the Pen (al-Qalam), the Tablet (al-Lawh), and the Recording Angels (al-Katibun). It follows a consistent pattern: each entity is briefly described, and then it is stated that we refrain from making a definitive judgment about its true reality due to lack of knowledge. The ‘Arsh is said to be the first created entity in a concrete sense (wujūdan ‘ayniyyan). The Kursi is a luminous body between the hands of the ‘Arsh, attached to it above the seventh heaven, and it is distinct from the ‘Arsh, contrary to the view of al-Hasan al-Basri. The Pen is a luminous body that God created and commanded to write all that has happened and will happen until the Day of Judgment. The writing angels are of three types: those who record human deeds, those who copy from the Preserved Tablet into the scrolls of angels entrusted with managing the world, and those who write from the scrolls of the guardian angels a book placed under the ‘Arsh. The Tablet is a luminous body on which the Pen wrote by God's permission all that was and will be until the Hour. The passage emphasizes that we cannot know the exact reality of these entities and must refrain from speculation.

Misconception: That we can fully know the reality of these entities through reason or speculation.
Correction: The text repeatedly states that we refrain from definitively determining their reality due to lack of knowledge, teaching that their true nature is known only to Allah.

Key Takeaway

The Wisdom Behind All Creation
Defines 'ḥikam' and asserts purpose in creation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that everything Allah created has a wisdom and benefit known to Him, even if our intellects cannot grasp it.

Core Idea
Every creation has a divine purpose known only to Allah.

This lesson begins a new section on sam‘iyyāt — matters known through revelation. The author first defines the term 'ḥikam' and establishes the foundational principle that nothing in creation is without purpose, even if that purpose lies beyond human comprehension.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage defining ḥikam
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Notice the definition of ḥikam as correctness or placing things in their proper place.
The term ḥikam is plural of ḥikmah.
2
Understand the concept of wisdom
Reflect on the two definitions: correctness/soundness and placing things in their proper place. Both emphasize purpose and order in creation.
3
Reflect on the limitation of human intellect
The passage states that even if our intellects fall short, Allah acts with wisdom and as He wills. Ask yourself: Why is it important to affirm wisdom beyond human understanding?
This connects to divine transcendence and trust in Allah's actions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قسم السمعيات كُلُّ حِكَمُ جمع حِكْمَة، وهي: صواب الأمر وسَدَاده ، أو وضع الشَّيء في موضعه ، أي : مَا خُلِق كلُّ واحدٍ منها إلَّا لحكمة وفائدة يعلمها الله ، وإِنْ قَصُرتْ عُقولنا عن الوقوف عليها ؛ لأنَّهُ تعالى يتصرَّفُ بما يشاءُ وافق الغرض أَوْ لَا . ١٠٨. لَا لِاخْتِيَاجِ وبها الإِيمَانُ يَجِبْ عَلَيكَ أَيُّهَا الإِنْسَانُ لَا لِاحْتِيَاج ، أي : لم يخلقها لاحتياج منه إليها في اكتنان، ولا في جلوس، ولا في ضبط ما يخافُ نسيانه ، ولا استحصال ما غاب عن علمه تعالى الله عن ذلك علوا كبيرًا وبها الإِيمَانُ أي: ولكنَّها كغيرها ممَّا ثبت الأحاديث ، كالحُجُبِ والأنوار يَجِبْ التصديق بوجودها شَرعا ، بصحيح
Section on sam‘iyyāt (things heard/revealed). Every wisdom (ḥikam) — plural of ḥikmah, and it is the correctness and soundness of a matter, or placing a thing in its proper place — meaning: each one of them was not created except for a wisdom and benefit that God knows, even if our intellects fall short of grasping it, because He Almighty acts as He wills, whether it aligns with the purpose or not. 108. Not out of need, and through them faith is obligatory upon you, O man. (Not out of need) i.e., He did not create them out of any need from Him to them in concealment, nor in sitting, nor in preserving what He fears to forget, nor in obtaining what was hidden from His knowledge — God is exalted above that with a great exaltation. And through them faith, i.e., but they are like other matters established by authentic hadith, such as the veils and lights. Faith in their existence is obligatory by Shari‘a, on the basis of sound (reports).
Source pages p. 545

Commentary
This passage begins a new section on sam‘iyyāt (matters known through revelation). It first defines the word 'ḥikam' (wisdoms) as either the correctness of an affair or placing a thing in its proper place. It then explains that every created thing was created only for a wisdom and benefit known to God, even if our intellects cannot grasp it, because God acts as He wills, whether it aligns with our purpose or not. The poem line states: 'Not out of need, and through them faith is obligatory upon you, O man.' The commentary elaborates: God did not create these things out of any need on His part, such as needing a screen (iktinān) or a seat (julūs), nor out of fear of forgetting, nor to obtain knowledge of what was unknown to Him — God is exalted above all that. Rather, faith in them is just like faith in other unseen matters established by authentic hadith, such as the veils (al-ḥujub) and lights (al-anwār). Believing in their existence is obligatory by the Shari‘a, based on sound texts.

Correction: The passage teaches that everything has a wisdom and benefit known to Allah, but our intellects may fall short of grasping it. We must affirm divine wisdom even when we cannot perceive it.

Wisdom Behind Creation and Obligation of Belief in the Unseen
Explains that all creation has divine wisdom and belief is obligatory even if wisdom is unknown.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that every creation has divine wisdom known only to Allah, and that belief in revealed matters is a devotional obligation independent of our intellectual grasp.

Core Idea
Allah creates with wisdom, not need; our duty is to believe, not to fully comprehend.

This lesson explores why Allah created everything. The author explains that every created thing has a purpose known to Allah, even if our minds cannot fathom it. Moreover, we are required to believe in matters of revelation simply because they are from Allah, not because we understand them. This establishes a key principle: faith is submission to divine wisdom, not intellectual comprehension.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to understand the overall argument about divine wisdom and belief in the unseen.
Notice how the author defines wisdom and then negates any need in Allah.
2
Understand the definition of wisdom
Grasp the meaning of 'hikma' as correctness and placing things in their proper place. This sets the stage for understanding that creation has purpose.
3
Analyze the negation of need
Examine the statement 'Not due to need' which refutes any anthropomorphic notion that Allah creates out of necessity. Understand why this is crucial for tawhid.
Allah is free from need in concealment, sitting, memory, or knowledge.
4
Recognize the obligation of belief
Understand that belief in matters of revelation (sam'iyyat) is obligatory as a devotional act, even if we cannot comprehend their full wisdom.
Faith in hadith-revealed entities like veils and lights is required.
5
Reflect on the devotional nature of faith
Consider how this principle guards against the misconception that faith requires intellectual mastery. Instead, it is ta'abbudī (devotional submission).

Division of Sam'iyyat (Matters Known from Revelation). *(Every wisdom)* plural of wisdom, which is: correctness and rightness of the affair, or placing a thing in its proper place. That is: each one of them was not created except for a wisdom and benefit that Allah knows, even if our intellects fall short of perceiving them; because He, exalted, acts as He wills, whether it coincides with the purpose or not. 108. Commentary
This passage is an exposition on the nature of created things and the obligation of belief in matters known through revelation (sam'iyyat). It begins by defining 'wisdom' (hikma) as correctness or placing something in its proper place, then clarifies that every created thing has a divine purpose known only to Allah, even if our intellects cannot grasp it, because Allah acts as He wills without constraint. The poem line 'Not due to need...' negates any attribution of need to Allah in creation—He did not create things like the Throne, Pen, or other revealed objects out of any need for concealment, sitting, memory preservation, or knowledge acquisition; He is far above such needs. Instead, the imperative to believe in them is purely legal (shar'ī) based on authentic hadiths, not on rational comprehension. The commentary stresses that this faith is ta'abbudī (devotional), meaning we affirm without grasping the underlying rationale, guarding against anthropomorphic or necessitarian misconceptions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That God creates things out of need or that belief requires full intellectual understanding of divine purposes.
Correction: The passage explicitly negates any need in Allah and establishes that belief is devotional (ta'abbudī), affirming without comprehending the wisdom.

According to the passage, why were created things brought into existence?
A) For a wisdom and benefit known to Allah.
B) Because Allah needed them for concealment or sitting.
C) So that humans can fully comprehend their purpose.
D) For no reason at all.

Key Takeaway
All creation is for a divine purpose, and belief in revelation is a devotional duty, not dependent on rational comprehension.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face a situation in life that seems pointless or unjust, do you instinctively demand an explanation from Allah, or do you submit to His wisdom even when you cannot see it? How can you train yourself to adopt the latter attitude based on this lesson?
?
Are there Islamic beliefs you hold primarily because they make sense to you rationally, rather than because Allah commanded them? What would it take for you to believe simply out of obedience, even if your mind struggles?
?
Consider something in creation (e.g., a trial or a commandment) that you find difficult to accept. Does the fact that Allah knows the wisdom of it, while you do not, change your response? What concrete step can you take this week to act on that belief?

Reality of Hellfire and Obligation of Belief
Affirms Hellfire's reality and obligatory belief.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that Hellfire is a true, created reality that every Muslim must believe in as established by the Quran, Sunnah, and scholarly consensus.

Core Idea
Hellfire is real, created, and obligatory to believe in.

This lesson opens by affirming the reality of Hellfire as a fundamental tenet of faith. The poem line states that Hellfire is true (ḥaqq) and created like Paradise, warning against denial. The commentary explains that this truth is established by divine revelation and scholarly consensus, making belief in it obligatory for every Muslim.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then the English translation. Notice the poem's direct assertion and the commentary's justification.
The passage begins with the heading about obligation of belief.
2
Identify the key claim
The central claim is that Hellfire is 'true' (ḥaqq). What does 'true' mean here? It means established by revelation and consensus.
3
Understand the proofs
The commentary lists three sources: the Quran, the Sunnah, and the consensus of scholars. These are the foundations for the reality of Hellfire.
Consensus of Ahl al-Sunna is emphasized.
4
Connect to obligation
Because it is established by these sources, belief in Hellfire is wajib (obligatory). The passage warns against denying it.
Denial is associated with madness (jinna).
5
Reflect on the warning
The poem cautions: 'do not incline to a denier possessed of madness.' This underscores the seriousness of denying Hellfire.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وجوب الإيمان بالجنة والنار وخلودهما]
١٠٩. والنَّارُ حقٌّ أُوجِدَتْ كَالْجَنَّةِ
فَلَا تَمِلْ لِجَاحِدٍ ذِي جِنَّةِ
(وَالنَّارُ حَقٌّ) أي ثَابتةٌ بالكتاب والسُّنَّة واتفاق عُلماء الأُمَّة ، وكلُّ ما هو كذلك .. فالإيمان به واجب ، إلى هذا ذهبَ جمهورُ أهل السُّنَّة (۱) والمُراد مِن النَّار: دارُ العذابِ بجميع طبقاتها السبع التي أعلاها جهنّم (۲) ، وتحتها لَظَى ، ثُمَّ الحُطَمَة ، ثُمَّ السَّعيرُ ، ثُمَّ سَقَر ، ثُمَّ الجَحِيمُ ، ثُمَّ الهَاوِيَة ، وبابُ كلّ واحدة (۳) من داخل الأخرى على الاستواء، وبين أعلى جهنّم وأسفلها خمس وسبعمئة سنة ، وحَرُّها (٤) هواءٌ مُحرِقٌ ، ولا جَمر لها سوى بني آدم والأحجار المُتَّخَذَةِ آلِهَةٌ مِن دون الله .
[Obligation of Belief in Paradise and Hell and their Eternity] 109. And the Hellfire is true, created like Paradise, so do not incline to a denier possessed of madness. (And the Hellfire is true), i.e., established by the Book, the Sunnah, and the consensus of the scholars of the Umma, and everything that is so... belief in it is obligatory; to this went the majority of Ahl al-Sunna. And what is meant by the Hellfire: the abode of punishment with all its seven layers, the highest of which is Jahannam, beneath it Laza, then al-Hutama, then al-Sa'ir, then Saqar, then al-Jahim, then al-Hawiya. The door of each one is inside the other on the same level, and between the top of Jahannam and its bottom is five hundred and seventy years. Its heat is burning air, and it has no ember except the sons of Adam and the stones taken as gods besides Allah.
Source pages p. 545

Commentary
This passage is a doctrinal assertion regarding the reality of Hellfire and Paradise. It opens with the poem line stating that Hellfire is true (ḥaqq) and created like Paradise, warning against denying it. The commentary explains that 'true' means it is established by the Quran, Sunnah, and consensus of the scholars, and therefore belief in it is obligatory upon every Muslim, as held by the majority of Ahl al-Sunna. It then defines Hellfire as the abode of punishment with seven layers in descending order: Jahannam (the highest), Laza, al-Hutama, al-Sa'ir, Saqar, al-Jahim, and al-Hawiya (the lowest). The doors of each layer are within another on the same level, and the vertical distance from top to bottom is 570 years. Its heat is described as burning air, and its fuel consists of humans and the stones that were worshipped as gods. This affirms a literal, physical Hell, rejecting metaphorical interpretations or denial.

The Seven Layers of Hellfire and Its Fuel
Describes the seven layers, doors, distance, heat, and fuel of Hellfire.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to name the seven layers of Hellfire in order and describe its fuel and physical characteristics.

Core Idea
Hellfire has seven layers, each with its own door, and its fuel is humans and idolatrous stones.

After establishing the reality of Hellfire, this lesson describes its physical structure: seven layers in descending order, with doors inside each other. It also reveals the terrifying fuel of Hellfire: human beings and the stones that were worshipped as gods.

Guided Path
1
Read the description of layers
Read the Arabic passage and translation carefully. Note the list of names and the details about doors, distance, heat, and fuel.
The passage starts with 'And what is meant by the Hellfire...'
2
Memorize the layers in order
The seven layers from top to bottom are: Jahannam, Laza, Hutama, Sa'ir, Saqar, Jahim, Hawiya. Try to learn this sequence.
Jahannam is the highest, Hawiya the lowest.
3
Understand the door arrangement and distance
The door of each layer is inside the next on the same level. The vertical distance from top to bottom is 570 years of travel.
4
Note the nature of heat and fuel
Its heat is burning air (not conventional fire), and its fuel consists of humans and stones that were worshipped as gods.
This highlights the severity and specific purpose.
5
Reflect on the implications
Consider why the fuel includes idolatrous stones and humans. This ties to the sin of shirk and the severe consequences.
