إيمان
حَتْم
سمعي
نقل
جاحِد

الفسق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Hawd is a metaphorical symbol, not a real physical pool.
Correction: The text affirms it as a specific large body with clear dimensions and properties, and its denial is a blameworthy innovation.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway

Obligation to Believe in the Prophet's Basin
States the obligation to believe in the basin and discusses its description and location.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that belief in the Prophet's basin is obligatory, its described attributes, how to reconcile different reports about its size, and that not knowing its chronological order does not harm faith.

Core Idea
Belief in the basin is obligatory; its exact timing is not essential.

This passage from the Jawhara establishes the obligation to believe in the Prophet's basin (al-hawd), a heavenly fountain exclusive to the Prophet Muhammad. It presents a vivid hadith description, reconciles varying reports about its dimensions, and clarifies that only belief in its existence is required — not knowledge of its sequence relative to other eschatological events.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that the passage begins with the obligation statement.
2
Identify the obligation and description
The passage states that belief in the basin is obligatory. Then it quotes a hadith describing its size, water, smell, vessels, and the effect of drinking from it.
The hadith from 'Amr ibn al-'As emphasizes the vastness and qualities of the basin.
3
Understand the reconciliation
Follow how the passage harmonizes different narrations about the basin's dimensions—either tailored to audiences or gradual revelation. Finally, note the ruling that ignorance of its chronological order relative to the Sirat does not harm belief.
The reconciliation highlights that reliance is on the longest distance, as per al-Nawawi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وجوب الإيمان بحوض سيد الأنبياء. عمرو بن العاص: حوضي مسيرة شهر وزواياه سواء، ماؤه أبيض من اللبن، وريحه أطيب من المسك، وكيزانه أكثر من نجوم السماء، من شرب منه فلا يظمأ أبداً. وما ورد من تحديده بجهات مختلفة إما بحسب من حضره ممن يعرف تلك الجهة؛ فخاطب كل قوم بالجهة التي يعرفونها، أو أنه أخبر أولا بالمسافة اليسيرة، ثم أُعلِمَ بالمسافة الطويلة، فأخبر بها، كأن الله سبحانه تفضل عليه باتساعه شيئا فشيئا؛ فيكون الاعتماد على ما يدل على أطولها مسافة، كما أشار إليه النووي رحمه الله تعالى، وفيما أوحى الله إلى عيسى من صفة نبينا: له حوض أبعد من مكة إلى مطلع الشمس، فيه آنية مثل عدد نجوم السماء، وله لون كل شراب الجنة وطعم كل ثمار الجنة. وظواهر الأحاديث أنه بجانب الجنة كما قاله ابن حجر، والواجب اعتقاد ثبوته، وجهل تقدمه على الصراط أو تأخره لا يضر بالاعتقاد.
Obligation of belief in the basin of the master of prophets. 'Amr ibn al-'As: My basin is a month's journey, its corners are equal, its water is whiter than milk, its smell is more fragrant than musk, and its vessels are more numerous than the stars of the sky; whoever drinks from it will never thirst again. And what has been reported of defining it with different directions—either according to those present who know that direction, so he addressed each people by the direction they know, or that he first informed of the short distance, then was informed of the long distance, so he informed of it, as if Allah the Exalted favored him by its expansion little by little; so reliance is upon what indicates its longest distance, as indicated by al-Nawawi, may Allah have mercy on him. And in what Allah revealed to Jesus describing our Prophet: he has a basin farther than Mecca to the rising of the sun, containing vessels like the number of the stars of the sky, and having the color of every drink of Paradise and the taste of every fruit of Paradise. And the apparent meanings of the hadiths are that it is beside Paradise, as Ibn Hajar said. And it is obligatory to believe in its existence, and ignorance of its precedence over the Sirat or its delay does not harm belief.
Source pages p. 552

Commentary
This passage defines the obligation to believe in the Prophet's basin (al-hawd). It begins by stating that belief in it is obligatory. Then it cites a hadith from 'Amr ibn al-'As describing the basin's size, water, smell, vessels, and the effect of drinking from it. Next, it addresses the different narrations about the basin's dimensions and locations, reconciling them by suggesting the Prophet tailored descriptions to his audience or received progressive revelations. The author concludes that the correct distance is the longest, as per al-Nawawi. A further revelation to Jesus is mentioned, emphasizing the basin's vastness. The apparent meaning of hadiths places the basin beside Paradise, but the author clarifies that only belief in its existence is obligatory; not knowing whether it comes before or after the Sirat does not harm one's faith.

Key Terms
الحوض
الصراط
الميزان
السمعيات
الإيمان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That one must know the exact chronological order of eschatological events, specifically whether the basin comes before or after the Sirat.
Correction: The passage explicitly states that ignorance of this order does not harm belief.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling regarding knowledge of whether the basin comes before or after the Sirat?
A) It is obligatory to know.
B) Ignorance of it does not harm belief.
C) It is a severe sin to be ignorant.
D) It is a matter of ijtihad.

Key Takeaway
It is obligatory to believe in the Prophet's basin, but one's faith is not harmed by not knowing whether it precedes or follows the Sirat.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly long to drink from the Prophet's basin? What in your life right now might prevent you from being among those who drink from it? What will you change today to increase your hope and preparation?
?
If the basin's exact timing is not required for belief, why do you sometimes get caught up in arguing about details of the afterlife instead of focusing on the state of your own heart and actions? Will you commit to prioritizing inner purification over theological debate?
?
The basin's water is described as pure, fragrant, and thirst-quenching. Is your heart as pure and your deeds as fragrant in the sight of Allah? If the Prophet were to see your life today, would he be pleased to welcome you to his basin? What one step will you take this week to purify your intentions?

Unseen Matters
beginner

Who Drinks from the Basin and Who Is Repelled
Explains verse 112 on the basin, covenant, and tawatur.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the explanation of verse 112 regarding the Prophet's basin, including who will drink from it and who will be repelled, and the basis for belief in these reports.

Core Idea
The basin is for covenant-keepers; transgressors are repelled.

This passage unpacks the meaning of a line from the poem that describes the events at the Prophet's basin on the Day of Judgment. It clarifies who will be allowed to drink and who will be prevented, grounding the discussion in the hadith corpus that reports these events.

Guided Path
1
Read the verse and explanation
Begin by reading the verse in Arabic and its literal translation. Notice the structure: it is part of the Sam'iyyat (matters of the unseen).
2
Understand the covenant
The 'covenant' (al-ʿahd) refers to the primordial pact taken from all souls. Those who fulfill it die in faith without changing or altering.
The passage notes this description could include previous nations, but hadith limit the basin to this Ummah.
3
Distinguish the Prophet's basin
Why is our Prophet's basin specially mentioned? Because its reports are mutawatir (mass-transmitted), while others are ahad (single-chain). This is a key point about how we know such matters.
4
Identify the repelled
Those repelled are people who changed and altered the covenant, i.e., abandoned Islam after it reached them. Allah accepts no other religion from such a person.
5
Recognize the obligation
The passage concludes that belief in these reports is obligatory because they reach the level of moral tawatur (overwhelming certainty).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قسم السمعيات
عنه بِعَهْدِهِمْ وَقُلْ يُذَادُ مَنْ طَغَوا ١١٢ - يَنَالُ شُرْبًا مِنْهُ أَقْوَامٌ وَفَوا
( يَنَالُ شُرْبًا مِنْهُ) أي: يتعاطى الشرب من ذلك الحوض لدفع العطش، أو للتلذذ، أو لتعجيل المسرة (أَقْوَامٌ وَفَوْا) الله تعالى (بِعَهْدِهِمْ) وهو الميثاق الذي أخذه الله عليهم في الإيمان به، وباليوم الآخر، واتباع دينه وشرائعه، وتصديق كتبه ورسله، حين أخرجهم من ظهر آدم، وأشهدهم على أنفسهم، فماتوا على ذلك لم يغيروا ولم يبدلوا، وهذا الوصف وإن شمل الأمم السابقة لكنه خلاف ظواهر الأحاديث أنه لا يرده إلا مؤمنو جميع مؤمني هذه الأمة؛ لأن كل أمة إنما ترد حوض نبيها (1)، وتخصيص حوض نبينا بالذكر لوروده بالأحاديث البالغة مبلغ التواتر، بخلاف غيره لوروده بالآحاد. (وَقُلْ يُذَادُ) أي: يطرد عنه، فلا يشرب منه (مَنْ طَغَوْا) أي: أقوام غيروا وبدلوا عهدهم الذي أخذه الله عليهم، وهو الإسلام الذي ألزمهم اتباعه، ولم يقبل ممن بلغه دينا غيره (2)، كما وردت بذلك الآثار الصحيحة والحسنة البالغ مجموعها مبلغ التواتر المعنوي، وكل ما هو كذلك فالإيمان به واجب.
(1) قوله: (إنما ترد حوض نبيها) لما ورد عن الحسن مرفوعا: «إن لكل نبيا حوضا، وهو قائم على حوضه وبيده عصا يدعو من عرف من أمته، ألا وإنهم يتباهون أيهم أكثر تبعا، وإني لأرجو أن أكون أكثرهم تبعا» الشنواني. والحديث عند الترمذي بلفظ قريب.
(2) قوله: (ولم يقبل ممن بلغه دينا غيره) عطف على قوله: (ألزمهم اتباعه) أي: ولم يقبل الله من شخص بلغه دين الإسلام دينا غيره الشنواني.
Section of the Sam'iyyat. From it: with their covenant, and say: those who transgress are repelled. 112 - They obtain a drink from it, a people who fulfilled. (They obtain a drink from it) means: they take the drink from that basin to repel thirst, or for pleasure, or to hasten joy. (A people who fulfilled) Allah Almighty (their covenant) which is the covenant that Allah took from them to believe in Him, the Last Day, and to follow His religion and laws, and to believe in His books and messengers, when He brought them out from the back of Adam and made them testify against themselves, and they died upon that without changing or altering. This description, although it includes previous nations, contradicts the apparent meanings of the hadiths that none come to it except all believers of this nation; because every nation only comes to the basin of its own prophet (1), and the specification of our Prophet's basin by mention is because it is reported through hadiths that reach the level of tawatur, unlike others which are reported through ahad. (And say: those who transgress are repelled) means: they are driven away from it, so they do not drink from it (those who transgress) meaning: people who changed and altered their covenant which Allah took from them, which is Islam that He obligated them to follow, and He does not accept from one who has received it any other religion (2), as has been reported through authentic and good narrations whose total reaches the level of moral tawatur, and everything that is so, belief in it is obligatory. (1) His statement: (Only comes to the basin of its prophet) because of what has been reported from al-Hasan raised: 'Indeed every prophet has a basin, and he stands at his basin with a staff in his hand calling those he knows from his nation, and indeed they boast about who has more followers, and I hope to be the one with the most followers' - al-Shanwani. The hadith is in al-Tirmidhi with a similar wording. (2) His statement: (And He does not accept from one who has received it any other religion) is conjoined to his statement: (He obligated them to follow it) meaning: and Allah does not accept from a person who has received the religion of Islam any other religion - al-Shanwani.
Source pages p. 553

Commentary
This passage explains verse 112 of the poem. It is part of the section on Sam'iyyat (matters known through revelation). The verse says: 'They obtain a drink from it, a people who fulfilled their covenant, and say: those who transgress are repelled.' The commentary proceeds in order: first, 'they obtain a drink from it' is explained as taking the drink to quench thirst, seek pleasure, or hasten joy. Second, 'a people who fulfilled their covenant with Allah' refers to the primordial covenant (mithaq) that Allah took from all souls when they were created from the loins of Adam, testifying to faith and obedience. They died faithful without change. Although this description could include previous nations, the apparent meaning of hadiths is that only the believers of this Ummah will come to this particular basin, because each nation goes to its own prophet's basin. The basin of our Prophet is singled out because its reports are mutawatir, while reports of other basins are ahad. Third, 'and say: those who transgress are repelled' means they are driven away and prevented from drinking. They are those who changed and altered their covenant, meaning they abandoned Islam. Allah does not accept any other religion from someone who has received Islam. The passage concludes that such reports, even if not individually mutawatir, are collectively mutawatir in meaning, and belief in them is obligatory. Two footnotes elaborate: one quotes a hadith that every prophet has a basin; the other clarifies that Allah does not accept any religion other than Islam from those who have received it.

Key Terms
الحوض
العهد
الطغيان
التواتر
الآحاد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the verse applies to all nations equally.
Correction: The commentary specifies that the primary referent is this Ummah due to the abundance of evidence (tawatur) regarding the Prophet's basin.

Checkpoint
Who are the people who will be repelled from the basin according to the passage?
A) Those who have not fulfilled their covenant.
B) Those who have changed and altered their covenant.
C) All non-Muslims.
D) Only the sinners of the Muslim community.

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's basin is reserved for those who keep the covenant of faith, while transgressors who alter it are denied.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you consider the covenant Allah made with you before you were born, how have you fulfilled it today in your choices? What one specific action can you take this week to live by that covenant more sincerely?
?
If you were to stand before the Prophet's basin tomorrow, would you be among those who drink or among those who are repelled? What evidence from your daily life supports your answer?
?
You have heard that the hadith about the basin are mutawatir—certain and true. Do you truly believe in the basin with certainty, or is it just a distant concept? What would change in your life if you really lived as if you might be denied that drink?
